# Changelog

All notable changes to this project will be documented in this file.

The English section comes first, followed by a Japanese translation.
The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/), and this project adheres to [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).

## English

### [Unreleased]

#### Fixed
- **C# declaration-pattern and dotted receiver shadowing no longer leak phantom enum-member edges (#510, #511, #555, #561, #565, #569, #570, #574)** — `ReferenceExtractor` now treats declaration-pattern variables as scoped value receivers across wrapped `if` / `while` headers, conditional-expression true branches, `switch` case arms, switch-expression recursive/property pattern arms such as `Holder { Ready: > 0 } Status => ...`, single-line and multi-line recursive/property patterns such as `Holder { Ready: > 0 } Status`, dotted qualifiers whose first segment is a value receiver, and declaration-pattern variables introduced inside plain or `static` lambdas nested in conditional headers. This stops false `call` edges from `Status.Ready` after declaration-pattern binding, from receiver chains like `RealNs.Status.Ready` when `RealNs` is a parameter/property rather than a namespace/type qualifier, and from lambda-contained declaration patterns incorrectly hiding or inventing enum-member edges in surrounding scopes. Added extractor and CLI regressions covering same-line and multi-line declaration-pattern cases, lambda-contained declaration patterns, `switch`/`case`, switch expressions, conditional expressions, recursive/property patterns, `static` lambdas, and dotted receiver chains while preserving real enum-member references later in the same member. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #510, #511, #555, #561, #565, #569, #570, #574.
- **C# `global::Enum.Member` references now keep true global-escape semantics across shadowing and alias collisions (#531, #547)** — `ReferenceExtractor` now preserves an explicit leading `global::` qualifier through C# qualified-access parsing, skips both the value-receiver shadow filter and `using`-alias rewriting for that escape form, and therefore keeps `global::Color.Red` / `global::Demo.Color.Red` bound to the real global namespace even when the surrounding scope contains a same-named property, local, or alias. This also stops compile-invalid alias-only forms such as `global::Color.Red` from being rewritten into real enum-member edges via alias resolution. Added extractor and CLI regressions covering `references` and `inspect` for property-shadow, conflicting-alias, and alias-only-invalid cases. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #531, #547.
- **C# same-line generic brace-bodied members now restart sibling scans in the correct column domain (#533)** — `SymbolExtractor` now translates single-line C# brace-body end columns between raw-source and collapsed match-line coordinates before slicing signatures or restarting same-line sibling scans, so fixtures like `void M<T1,           T2>() { }int P { get; }event System.Action<int,           string> E;` keep the method signature bounded at its own body and still expose later property/event siblings. Added regression coverage in `SymbolExtractorTests`. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #533.
- **Windows CI now pins `TMP`/`TEMP` to `RUNNER_TEMP` before restore/build/test so temp-heavy fixtures avoid the slower default profile temp path (#527)** — The Windows `Build and Test` and `Release` workflows already carried Defender exclusions from #394, but the test suite still routes most temp projects/DBs through `Path.GetTempPath()`, which kept landing under the default user-profile temp root on hosted runners. Both workflows now create a dedicated `RUNNER_TEMP\cdidx-temp` directory, export it through `GITHUB_ENV` before the Defender-exclusion step, and log the effective `TMP`/`TEMP` plus `.NET` `Path.GetTempPath()` resolution. This keeps the temp-heavy test churn on the same CI-owned volume as the workspace and ensures the later Defender verification step checks the actual effective temp root rather than stale defaults. Affected: `.github/workflows/dotnet.yml`, `.github/workflows/release.yml`. Closes #527, #530.
- **Same-line C# type bodies now preserve mixed-member siblings across property/event shapes (#472)** — `SymbolExtractor` now rejects outer-type brace-property false positives by restarting from the first member inside the same-line type body instead of the regex tail, defers C# function/property same-line advancement when the current statement start is itself a property/event/delegate declaration, and restarts the full pattern list after same-line property/event/delegate declarations reach a later sibling so earlier regex rows can still see that sibling. Exact duplicate symbol rows are also suppressed when same-line restart paths revisit the same declaration, and C# same-line `event` / `delegate` signatures are now clamped at the declaration terminator instead of absorbing the enclosing type's closing brace. Compact fixtures such as `public class C { public int A => 1; public int P { get; set; } }`, `public class C { public int P { get; set; } public void M() { } }`, `public class C { public int P { get; set; } public event System.EventHandler E; }`, and `public class C { public event System.EventHandler E; public void M() { } }` now emit the expected symbols exactly once. Added regression coverage in `SymbolExtractorTests`. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #472.
- **C# same-line mixed member streams no longer drop earlier siblings behind later pattern families (#473)** — `SymbolExtractor` now treats compact same-line C# type-body members as a statement stream instead of letting earlier pattern families scan past sibling boundaries, so shapes like `event E; public int P { get; set; }`, `void M(); int P { get; }`, accessor-event forms like `event E { add {} remove {} } public int P { get; set; }`, and reverse-order `property + event` lines all emit each member with the correct same-line signature boundary. Added regression coverage for class/struct/interface mixed-kind fixtures, including accessor-event follow-up coverage from #520. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #473, #520.
- **C# same-line generic compact-member chains now keep both later brace-bodied signatures and compact-sibling restarts aligned (#525)** — `SymbolExtractor` now reuses the raw-column start position for same-line C# brace-body and wrapped-header signature slicing whenever the regex matched against the collapsed per-line generic buffer, so later siblings after `void M<T1, T2>(); event Action<int, string> E; ...` no longer keep phantom leading `;` / `{` in property or nested-interface signatures. The same fix set now also translates raw same-line brace endpoints back into the collapsed match-line column domain before restarting compact-sibling scans, so dense shapes like `void M<T1,           T2>() { }int P { get; }event ...` no longer drop `P` / `E` or absorb them into `M`'s signature. Added focused regression coverage for the direct property, nested-interface, and no-space compact-chain shapes. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #525, #533.
- **C# enum-member shadowing now uses offset-scoped lifetimes for same-line lambdas, query expressions, and brace-less embedded statements (#371)** — `ReferenceExtractor` no longer drops real enum-member references merely because a same-line lambda parameter, `foreach` variable, or LINQ range variable reuses the same identifier later on the line. Shadow scopes are now tracked by exact start/end offsets instead of line-wide suppression, parenthesized lambdas start at the actual `(` position, query range variables stop at the enclosing subexpression boundary, and brace-less `if/else` embedded statements are parsed as a single scope-bearing unit so later tails are not cut off. Added extractor and CLI regressions covering same-line lambda/foreach tails, query-in-argument cases, parenthesized lambda prefixes, and brace-less `if/else` forms. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #371.

### [1.13.0] - 2026-04-21

#### Changed
- **Distributed installs now keep persistent stderr breadcrumbs with 30-day retention** — `ProgramRunner` now enables `GlobalToolLog` for distributed/non-development executions and mirrors terminal stderr plus minimal lifecycle metadata into a per-user daily file named `stderr-YYYYMMDD.log`. Repository-local development runs from `src/CodeIndex/bin/...` and `tests/.../bin/...` stay excluded by default so normal build/test cycles do not accumulate persistent logs. Default log roots are `%LOCALAPPDATA%\cdidx\logs\` on Windows, `~/Library/Logs/cdidx/` on macOS, and `$XDG_STATE_HOME/cdidx/logs/` (or `~/.local/state/cdidx/logs/`) on Linux. The log directory is pruned to the newest 30 daily files on startup, `CDIDX_DISABLE_PERSISTENT_LOG=1` disables the feature, and `CDIDX_GLOBAL_TOOL_LOG_DIR` remains available for test/packaging overrides. Added regression coverage for stderr mirroring, 30-file pruning, and explicit opt-out, and documented the behavior in the user and developer guides. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/GlobalToolLog.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ProgramRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ProgramRunnerTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`.
- **Interactive indexing/output no longer goes visually silent after `Indexing...`** — `IndexCommandRunner` now keeps a live `Indexing...` spinner active on interactive terminals during full-scan indexing work instead of stopping it before the first file and leaving the user with a fixed line until the next 50-file progress redraw or warning. Scoped update runs now also keep a live `Updating...` spinner under the same interactive-only contract, pausing only long enough to print `[WARN]`, `[OK]`, `[SKIP]`, `[DEL]`, `[ERR]`, or progress-bar output cleanly and then resuming immediately. Redirected stdout behavior is intentionally unchanged in shape: stdout still gets a single `Indexing...` banner plus line-based progress, while warnings stay on stderr, so logs/pipes do not collect spinner-frame noise. README examples now document both the interactive and redirected-output behavior, and `SELF_IMPROVEMENT.md` now explicitly treats visible liveness for long-running human-facing CLI flows as a regression bar. Added regression coverage ensuring redirected full-scan output prints `Indexing...` exactly once and redirected verbose update output does not duplicate the `Updating ... file(s)...` banner. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/IndexCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `README.md`, `SELF_IMPROVEMENT.md`.

#### Fixed
- **`callers` human output now surfaces grouped `reference_kind` tags without changing JSON (#383)** — `RunCallers` now prints each human-readable caller row with a leading grouped `reference_kind` tag so terminal users can distinguish `call`, `instantiate`, and `subscribe` edges without rerunning the command with `--json`. The read path now carries an internal grouped caller kind while keeping the serialized `CallerResult` JSON shape unchanged, and regression coverage locks a ctor-chain-plus-`new` fixture in `QueryCommandRunnerTests`. Documentation was updated in both README and DEVELOPER_GUIDE. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Models/QueryResults.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #383.
- **C# explicit-interface extraction no longer invents phantom methods from qualified `new Namespace.Type()` expressions (#362)** — The C# explicit-interface method regex now excludes `new` in the return-type position, so standalone constructor expressions such as `new System.Text.StringBuilder()` and `new System.Net.Http.HttpClient()` are no longer indexed as fake `function StringBuilder` / `function HttpClient` rows. Added extractor regression coverage that keeps real explicit-interface members such as `void IDisposable.Dispose()` working while suppressing the phantom constructor-name rows. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #362.
- **C# generic-over-tuple return types no longer disappear from symbol extraction (#344, #484)** — `SymbolExtractor` now treats embedded tuple groups inside C# type tokens as real return-type segments only when the parenthesized group is tuple-shaped (contains a comma at the outer tuple level), which lets ordinary methods, interface declarations, and explicit-interface implementations capture shapes such as `Task<(int, string)>`, `Dictionary<string, (int x, int y)>`, `IEnumerable<(string Key, int Value)>`, `List<(int, int)> IFoo.GetList()`, `Task<((int A, int B), string Name)>`, and `Task<(((int A, int B), int C), string Name)>` without reintroducing the primary-ctor / collection-expression false positives guarded by the existing `ReferenceExtractor` regression suite. Added regression coverage for the new generic-over-tuple cases plus the nearby primary-ctor and collection-expression cases that would otherwise misfire if non-tuple `(...)` groups were accepted too broadly. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #344, #484.
- **Same-line C# static constructors now surface before later sibling properties can short-circuit symbol extraction** — The dedicated C# static-constructor regex now runs before the brace/expression-bodied property rows, so compact one-line type bodies such as `public class E { static E() { } public int R { get; set; } }` emit both the static constructor and the later property instead of losing the ctor after the property row claims the later statement and stops the pattern scan. Added regression coverage that locks both instance/static same-line constructors and their later sibling auto-properties in one fixture. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #478.
- **DEVELOPER_GUIDE now keeps a single authoritative C# support row in both language tables (#483)** — Removed the duplicated older C# row from the English and Japanese "Supported symbol kinds by language" tables so each section keeps the newer constructor-lookahead wording in one canonical entry instead of two conflicting rows. Affected: `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #483.
- **Added explicit regression coverage for the existing C# complex enum-value fix (#357)** — Current `main` already indexes C# enum members whose assigned values start with member access, casts, parenthesized expressions, and framework constant lookups such as `K.Foo`, `(int)1.5`, `(1 + 2)`, `(int)'A'`, `System.Int32.MaxValue`, and `[Flags]` aliases like `Execute = K.Foo`, but the open issue's exact `E1` / `Permissions` dogfood fixture was not pinned end-to-end. Added an extractor-level regression that keeps those value shapes under `SymbolExtractorTests`, plus `QueryCommandRunner` integration coverage that indexes the same file and asserts both `symbols --json --exact-name` and `definition --json --exact-name` still resolve the affected members under the correct owning enum. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #357.
- **Added explicit regression coverage for the existing C# object-initializer phantom-enum fix (#374)** — Current `main` already suppresses object-initializer assignments such as `Age = 30,` and `Priority = 2` from reappearing as phantom C# enum members, but the open issue's exact dogfood fixture was not pinned end-to-end. Added an extractor-level regression that uses the full issue repro with both multiline and inline `new Person { ... }` initializers, plus a `QueryCommandRunner` integration test that round-trips the indexed file through `symbols --json --exact-name` and asserts `Age` / `Priority` resolve only to the real `Person` properties. This keeps issue #374 closable without relying on an older, narrower unit fixture alone. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #374.
- **C# interface and struct members now keep their immediate type container instead of falling back to the enclosing namespace** — `AssignContainers` now treats `interface` and `struct` symbols as container-stack candidates, so members such as interface events and struct properties/events inherit `container_kind` / `container_name` / `container_qualified_name` from the enclosing type rather than the surrounding namespace. Added regression coverage for the #466 interface-event repro and the same-root-cause struct-member case tracked in #468. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #466.
- **C# interface events now stay attached to their interface container in symbol output** — `AssignContainers` now treats `interface` and `struct` as real symbol containers instead of only `class` / `namespace` / `enum`, so members declared inside them inherit the innermost enclosing type instead of falling back to the surrounding namespace. This fixes the concrete `#334` dogfood fixture where `IBus.Regular`, `IBus.StaticAbs`, and `IBus.StaticVirt` were emitted as namespace-level events in `symbols`, `outline`, and `inspect`, and adds regression coverage that locks both the modifier acceptance and the interface container attribution in place. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #466.
- **Same-line C# type bodies now keep brace-body auto-properties instead of dropping them behind false outer-type matches** — `SymbolExtractor` now treats rejected C# brace-property false positives as same-line scan misses instead of terminal breaks, so lines like `public class C { public int P { get; set; } }`, `public struct S { public int Q { get; set; } }`, and `public interface I { int R { get; } }` advance past the outer type header and still emit the nested property. Container assignment now also recognizes `struct` and `interface` as same-line containers, so the recovered properties attach to `S` / `I` rather than falling back to the namespace. Added regression coverage for same-line class/struct/interface auto-properties plus same-line method/event controls. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #470.
- **`status --json` now exposes hotspot-family trust signals before `hotspots` runs (#460)** — `StatusResult` now carries `hotspot_family_ready` plus `hotspot_family_degraded_reason`, `DbReader.GetStatus()` populates those fields from the existing hotspot-family readiness signal, and the one-line status summary now marks the index as degraded when duplicate-name hotspot families are not yet authoritative. To keep the operational guidance consistent, `cdidx index` JSON/human readiness output and degraded-readiness warnings now surface the same hotspot-family trust bit as well. Added CLI and MCP regression coverage so automation can discover degraded hotspot-family metadata up front instead of probing `hotspots --json` first. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbWriter.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Models/QueryResults.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/IndexCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`, `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. Closes #460.
- **Nested generic C#/Java call sites no longer disappear from the reference index** — `ReferenceExtractor` now keeps the existing regex fast path for flat calls, then runs a depth-aware fallback scanner for nested-generic tails that end in `>>(` so outer constructor/method targets such as `new Dictionary<string, List<int>>()`, `new ArrayList<HashMap<String, Integer>>()`, and `Helper.DoWork<List<int>>()` still emit `instantiate` / `call` rows instead of silently dropping the entire call site. Added C# and Java regression coverage and documented the extraction rule in the developer docs. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. Closes #263.
- **C# symbol extraction no longer goes super-linear on `InstallScriptTests.cs`-style raw-string fixtures without truncating long field signatures** — `BuildCSharpPropertyMatchLine` now uses a bounded confirmation phase only for suspicious multiline field/property candidates, then switches to a linear continuation scan once the candidate is confirmed as a real declaration (`name = ...` or a named member header before `{`). That stops raw-string + heredoc bodies from triggering repeated whole-tail re-normalization across the rest of a large file, while still preserving full `symbols` / `definition` / `outline` signatures for wrapped raw-string fields, same-line `const` raw-string fields, and long object/collection initializers well past the 16-line confirmation budget. Added regression tests for the real `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/InstallScriptTests.cs` fixture, extractor-level >16-line raw-string/object-initializer signatures, and CLI-level `symbols` / `outline` round-tripping of long raw-string fields. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #447.
- **Full `cdidx index <projectPath>` runs now recover hotspot-family trust after metadata-only loss without forcing `--rebuild`** — Full-scan reuse is now gated per hotspot-family marker language instead of by a single global `skipped == 0` check. If the stored C#/VB/F# hotspot-family metadata is missing or stale, unchanged files in that language are reindexed during the next normal full scan so the authoritative `family_key` / `container_qualified_name` rows are regenerated and `hotspot_family_ready` is restamped. Unchanged files in other languages may still be reused, and already-current hotspot-family languages keep their trust even when unrelated marker files change. Added regression coverage for the `#459` shape where only the C# hotspot-family metadata is cleared and the next `cdidx index .` run must restore both the metadata and `hotspots --json` readiness on a partially skipped scan. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/IndexCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #459.

### [1.12.0] - 2026-04-19

#### Changed
- **Installer cloud documentation expanded for Claude Code *and* Codex cloud harnesses** — `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, and `CLOUD_BOOTSTRAP_PROMPT.md` now explicitly document that the published `install.sh` flow is intended for cloud AI coding containers beyond Claude Code (including Codex-style harnesses), with mirrored bilingual guidance for restricted-egress setups, mirror/proxy env vars, and built-in local self-test invocation. The new `--self-test-local-mirror` path now defaults to an isolated temporary install directory unless a **non-empty** `CDIDX_INSTALL_DIR` is explicitly set, so a mock self-test cannot silently overwrite an existing real `~/.local/bin/cdidx` even when `CDIDX_INSTALL_DIR=""` is present in the environment. It also validates local mirror startup on `127.0.0.1` before download begins, forces loopback traffic to bypass outbound proxies via `NO_PROXY` / `no_proxy` plus `curl --noproxy`, and reports mirror-specific startup failures with log tail output instead of misclassifying them as generic external network/proxy errors. Permission-denied loopback bind failures are now differentiated from "port already in use" failures, and the docs now call out the mirror/proxy env vars, the loopback-listen prerequisite, and `CDIDX_LOCAL_MIRROR_PORT`. Added regression coverage for isolated self-test installs, explicit install-dir override behavior, empty-string install-dir handling, configured mirror override URLs, loopback proxy bypass, custom-port wiring, permission-denied bind failures, and generic local-mirror startup diagnostics. Affected: `README.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CLOUD_BOOTSTRAP_PROMPT.md`, `install.sh`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/InstallScriptTests.cs`.
- **Installer 403 troubleshooting now distinguishes API lookup failures from tunnel-policy denies** — `install.sh` now gives concrete next steps for HTTP 403 during latest-release lookup and asset download (explicit version pinning, mirror API override, and upstream proxy allow-list guidance), and `CLOUD_BOOTSTRAP_PROMPT.md` now explicitly states that `CONNECT tunnel failed, response 403` across every candidate host is an egress-policy deny that route substitution alone cannot fix. Affected: `install.sh`, `CLOUD_BOOTSTRAP_PROMPT.md`.
- **Installer self-test refuses to overwrite a real install even when `CDIDX_INSTALL_DIR` is pre-exported** — `install.sh --self-test-local-mirror` previously honored an explicit non-empty `CDIDX_INSTALL_DIR` as-is, so users who pre-export `CDIDX_INSTALL_DIR=$HOME/.local/bin` for normal installs could silently replace their real `cdidx` binary with the mock payload (which only responds to `--version`). The self-test now detects risky install directories — well-known system paths (`/usr/local/bin`, `/usr/bin`, `/opt/homebrew/bin`, `/opt/local/bin`), `$HOME/.local/bin`, and any directory already containing a `cdidx` executable — and aborts with a clear message telling the operator to either unset `CDIDX_INSTALL_DIR` so the self-test runs in an isolated temp dir, or pass the new `--self-test-allow-overwrite` flag if they really want to inspect the mock layout in place. The escape hatch is intentionally CLI-only: `SELF_TEST_ALLOW_OVERWRITE=1` from the caller's environment is no longer inherited, so a stale env var in the user's shell or CI cannot silently reintroduce the bypass. Path comparison also strips trailing slashes before matching the well-known-path list, so `/usr/local/bin/` and `$HOME/.local/bin/` are treated identically to the no-slash forms instead of slipping past exact-string equality. `CLOUD_BOOTSTRAP_PROMPT.md` and `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md` document both the abort behavior and the escape hatch. Added regression coverage for the home-local-bin abort, the pre-existing-cdidx abort, a pre-exported `SELF_TEST_ALLOW_OVERWRITE=1` env var that must NOT bypass the guard, trailing-slash variants of every well-known system path and `$HOME/.local/bin/`, the CLI (`--self-test-allow-overwrite`) override, and a fresh custom dir that should pass through without the guard. Affected: `install.sh`, `CLOUD_BOOTSTRAP_PROMPT.md`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/InstallScriptTests.cs`.

#### Added
- **Batch (`.bat` / `.cmd`) labels and `set` variables now surface as symbols (#217)** — `LangMap` already recognized `.bat` / `.cmd` as language `batch` so the content was chunked and FTS-searchable, but `SymbolExtractor` had no `batch` pattern set at all, so every batch script — even substantial ones with half a dozen `:label` subroutines — indexed with zero symbol rows and `cdidx languages` showed `batch: Symbols: -`. Because batch labels (`:compile`, `:test`, `:deploy`, `:error`, `:end`, `:main`) are the only navigation anchors in a batch script — they are the targets of `goto :X` and `call :X` and effectively act as subroutine entry points — `symbols --lang batch`, `definition compile`, `outline build.bat`, and `inspect` all returned empty on Windows / cross-platform build scripts, installer driver scripts, and CI helpers. (`unused` is intentionally not claimed as a beneficiary here: batch remains `Graph = no` in the language pattern reference table — reference extraction is out of scope for this issue — so `unused --lang batch` would label every batch symbol as unused regardless of this fix. The scope of #217 is symbol visibility, not graph coverage.) Added a minimal `["batch"]` pattern set to `SymbolExtractor`: `^\s*:(?!eof(?![\w.-]))(?<name>[\w.\-]+)` captures labels as `function` symbols (the name character class naturally rejects the `::` / `:::` batch-comment forms because they have no label name; the case-insensitive `(?!eof(?![\w.-]))` negative lookahead excludes the reserved `:EOF` / `:eOf` / `:EoF` targets used by `goto :EOF` / `call :EOF` so they do not surface as phantom functions, while still allowing `eof`-prefixed user labels such as `:eof2` / `:eofish` / `:end-of-file` / `:eof.x` to pass; and the character class includes `.` so dotted labels such as `:build.release` are captured in full rather than truncated to `build`), and `^\s*(?:@\s*)?(?:if\s+.+?\s+)?set\s+(?:/[aApP]\s+)?""?(?<name>[A-Za-z_][\w]*)\s*(?:[+\-*/%&^|]|<<|>>)?=` captures `set VAR=value`, `set /a VAR=expr`, `set /p VAR=prompt`, and `set "VAR=value"` as `property` symbols, with `RegexOptions.IgnoreCase` so every compiler-legal casing (`SET`, `Set`, `SET /A`, `SET /P`, `Set /a`) is covered. The `(?:@\s*)?` prefix picks up echo-suppression forms (`@set FOO=1`, `@ SET FOO=2`), the `(?:if\s+.+?\s+)?` prefix picks up one-line conditional assignments (`if not defined OUTDIR set OUTDIR=%~dp0out`, `if "%1"=="" set X=default`), and the `(?:[+\-*/%&^|]|<<|>>)?=` tail picks up `set /a` compound arithmetic operators (`set /a COUNT+=1`, `set /A SHIFTED<<=2`). The leading anchor is also relaxed from `^\s*` to `(?:(?:^|&|\()\s*|(?:\belse|\bdo)\s+)` so same-line multi-statement forms emit one symbol per `set` occurrence instead of dropping every assignment after the first match: `set A=1 & set B=2`, `if exist foo.txt set C=3 & set D=4`, `if exist foo.txt ( set E=5 ) else set F=6`, and `for %%I in (1) do set LOOPVAR=%%I` all capture both (or all) variables. `rem` / `::` comment lines lack the required boundary token — they start with `r` or `:` rather than `^set` / `&set` / `(set` / `else set` / `do set` — so `rem set FAKE=...` and `:: set FAKE=...` still produce no phantom property symbol. The generic extractor loop normally stops after the first match per line for `BodyStyle.None`; a batch-specific branch advances `lineOffset` past the current match instead of short-circuiting so the same regex is re-applied against the rest of the line. Reference-extractor side (`goto :X` / `call :X`) remains out of scope for this fix and remains available as a follow-up; batch is still correctly listed without `Graph` support. Added a `SymbolExtractor` regression test `Extract_Batch_DetectsLabelsAndSetAssignments` that runs against CRLF-terminated input and uses `HashSet` equality assertions (not `Contains`) to pin the exact emitted-name set: every user label from the issue's repro (`main`, `compile`, `test`, `error`, `end`), every `set` variant across mixed casings (`VERSION`, `OUTPUT_DIR`, `/A COUNT`, `/P INPUT`, `"QUOTED"`), the `(?!eof(?![\w.-]))` boundary itself — `:eof2`, `:eofish`, and `:end-of-file` are included in the fixture and pinned in the expected function-name set so a future regression to `(?!eof)` or a plain `eof` string compare would be caught, the dotted-label contract — `:build.release` is included and pinned in the expected function-name set so a future regression to `[\w-]+` (which would truncate it to `build`) would be caught, the echo-suppression / compound-operator / inline-`if` property contracts — `@set AT_PREFIX=1`, `@ SET AT_SPACED=2`, `set /a COMPOUND+=1`, `set /A SHIFTED<<=2`, `if not defined INLINE_DEF set INLINE_DEF=inline_default`, and `if "%1"=="" set INLINE_EQ=empty` are included and pinned in the expected property-name set so a future regression that drops `@` prefix handling, compound-operator support, or inline-`if` support would be caught, and the same-line multi-statement contract — `set CHAIN_A=1 & set CHAIN_B=2`, `if exist foo.txt set IF_CHAIN_X=3 & set IF_CHAIN_Y=4`, `if exist foo.txt ( set PAREN_P=5 ) else set ELSE_Q=6`, `for %%I in (1) do set LOOPVAR=%%I` are included and their paired names (`CHAIN_A` / `CHAIN_B`, `IF_CHAIN_X` / `IF_CHAIN_Y`, `PAREN_P` / `ELSE_Q`, `LOOPVAR`) are pinned in the expected property-name set so a future regression that short-circuits after the first `set` on a line, or drops one of the boundary tokens (`&`, `(`, `else`, `do`), would be caught; `REM set FROM_REM=ignored` and `:: set FROM_DOUBLE_COLON=ignored` are also included in the fixture and deliberately absent from the expected set so a future regression that captures `set` inside comments would be caught. `:EOF` / `:eOf`, `::` line-comment, and `:::` triple-colon comment forms still never produce a phantom function symbol. Updated the `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md` language pattern reference table to move `batch` out of the "detected but not extracted" list and add it as a first-class row including the `property` column entries (`set VAR=`, `set /a VAR=` / `set /a VAR+=`, `set /p VAR=`, `set "VAR=..."`, `@set VAR=`, `if ... set VAR=`, and the same-line multi-statement forms `set A=1 & set B=2`, `( set X=1 )`, `if ... ( set P=1 ) else set Q=2`, `for ... do set VAR=`, with `rem` / `::` comment lines still excluded) and a `function` column that calls out both the "reserved `:EOF` excluded" carve-out and dotted-label support (`:name.sub`), and bumped the "languages with symbol extraction" count from 32 to 33 in both the English and Japanese sections; the `README.md` "supported languages" bullet list was also updated to add `Batch` and bump 32 → 33 in both sections. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `README.md`. Closes #217.
- **Installer `--reinstall-real <version>` validates a real release end-to-end without touching the user's real install** — `install.sh --reinstall-real vX.Y.Z` now downloads and installs the requested tag into an isolated `/tmp/cdidx-reinstall-real.XXXXXX` dir, runs `cdidx --version` and enumerates every `v<semver>` token in the output, requiring the one distinct token present to equal `v<requested>` so a mirror mixup, `version.json` skew, mixed-output diagnostic (e.g. `warning: requested version v1.2.3 not installed; running v9.9.9`), left-boundary violation (`prefixv1.2.3`), right-boundary violation (`v1.2.30`), or suffix mismatch (`v1.2.3` vs `v1.2.3-rc.1`) cannot silently pass. Token enumeration alone would still false-pass a diagnostic-only output whose single extracted token happens to equal the requested tag but does not represent the binary's own reported version (e.g. `see /releases/v1.2.3/notes for details` or `warning: expected package v1.2.3`), so `--reinstall-real` also requires the entire `cdidx --version` output to consist of EXACTLY one non-empty line and that line to match the literal form `cdidx v<requested>` verbatim — rejecting trailing-diagnostic shapes such as `cdidx v1.2.3 warning: expected package missing` whose single extracted token still equals the requested tag, and multi-line shapes such as `cdidx v1.2.3\nwarning: expected package v1.2.3 missing` where the exact first line would slip past a first-line-only check while a trailing diagnostic line still contains the same single distinct version token. It then builds a tiny scratch Python project in `/tmp/cdidx-reinstall-scratch.XXXXXX`, runs `cdidx . --db <scratch>/.cdidx/codeindex.db` against it, and runs `cdidx search greet --db <...>` to confirm indexing, native SQLite load, and FTS5 search still work on the freshly-downloaded binary. The search-output validation is a single awk state machine that couples the structured match header and the verbatim scratch source signature `def greet(name):` under EXACT full-line semantics: the single-line grep form is accepted only when the entire line is exactly `sample.py:<N>:def greet(name):` (end anchored — no trailing diagnostic prose, no space between the colon and the source signature), and the range form `^sample\.py:[0-9]+-[0-9]+$` (with nothing trailing) arms a one-shot "expect the first indented line" flag that is consumed on the very next two-space-indented line and accepts ONLY when that first indented line is exactly `  def greet(name):`. Any other line (blank, one-space, non-indented diagnostic, unrelated header, summary footer) clears the flag and abandons the block, so adjacency is strictly enforced. This full-line + first-indent coupling rejects the original split-evidence `sample.py:1-6` plus non-indented `warning: greet query returned 0 matches` shape, the header-inline diagnostic `sample.py:1-6 warning: greet query returned 0 matches` (previously matched via the loose `^sample\.py:[0-9]` + `greet` substring checks on the same line), the indented-diagnostic `sample.py:1-6\n  warning: greet query returned 0 matches` (previously matched the loose `^  .*greet` snippet check), the earlier `def greet`-bearing diagnostic shapes `sample.py:1: warning: expected code signature def greet missing` and `sample.py:1-6\n  warning: expected code signature def greet missing` (strict headers + diagnostics mentioning `def greet` without an argument list), and — crucially — three more residual shapes that a weaker substring match inside the match block would still false-pass: a grep-form header-line diagnostic whose prose embeds the FULL verbatim signature as a substring (`sample.py:1: warning: expected code signature def greet(name): missing`), a range-form indented-diagnostic whose prose embeds the FULL verbatim signature as a substring (`sample.py:1-6\n  warning: expected code signature def greet(name): missing`), and a range-form block whose first indented line is a non-matching decoy followed by a later indented `  def greet(name):` (`sample.py:1-6\n  warning: no matches\n  def greet(name):`) — all three are rejected because the grep form requires full-line equality and the range form consumes the one-shot adjacency flag on the very first indented line, never later. The full verbatim argument list `(name):` anchors the check against the actual scratch `sample.py` source rather than a substring that any diagnostic could counterfeit. Diagnostic text like `searching for greet returned 0 matches` and path-prefix false positives such as `other/sample.py:1` also remain rejected because the header regex is left-anchored and, for the range form, end-anchored. Human-readable output is used on purpose because trimmed release builds fail fast with exit code 4 on `--json`. `CDIDX_INSTALL_DIR` is intentionally ignored by this mode so a broken build can never clobber a working real install, and the temp install/scratch dirs are cleaned up on normal exit and on failure via `trap`. The `--self-test-local-mirror` mock only exercises `--version`, so regressions in indexing, version.json parsing, native library load, or search paths would previously slip through self-test; `--reinstall-real` closes that gap for pre-release validation. Added regression coverage for the missing-version-argument error, the `v` prefix normalization (`1.2.3` → `v1.2.3`), the isolated-tempdir guarantee when `CDIDX_INSTALL_DIR` points at `$HOME/.local/bin` (real install file must remain untouched), end-to-end invocation of `--version` / index / `search`, a broken-install simulation where the binary is missing after `main`, a search-failure path that aborts with a clear error, a version-mismatch stub that reports `v9.9.9` for a `v1.2.3` request, a left-boundary stub whose `--version` output is `prefixv1.2.3`, a trailing-digit stub whose output is `cdidx v1.2.30`, a mixed-output stub whose `--version` prints both `v1.2.3` and `v9.9.9` on one diagnostic line, a diagnostic-only stub whose `--version` output is `see /releases/v1.2.3/notes for details` (single token equals requested but not the real version line), a trailing-diagnostic stub whose `--version` output is `cdidx v1.2.3 warning: expected package missing` (first non-empty line starts with the expected prefix so a non-exact-match check would pass, and only one v<semver> token appears so token enumeration also passes), a `--json`-rejecting stub that reproduces the trimmed-release exit-4 behavior and confirms `--reinstall-real` no longer passes `--json`, an unstructured-search-output stub that prints `searching for greet returned 0 matches` so the validation correctly aborts instead of false-passing, a path-prefix search stub whose output contains `other/sample.py:1` plus a `greet` diagnostic to prove the anchored regex rejects it, a split-evidence search stub whose output is `sample.py:1-6` followed by a non-indented `warning: greet query returned 0 matches` diagnostic, a header-inline-diagnostic search stub whose single-line output is `sample.py:1-6 warning: greet query returned 0 matches` (greet token on the header line but no colon-after-line-number and no `def greet` signature), an indented-diagnostic search stub whose output is `sample.py:1-6` followed by a two-space-indented `warning: greet query returned 0 matches` (indented greet that is not real Python source), a multi-line-version stub whose `--version` output is `cdidx v1.2.3\nwarning: expected package v1.2.3 missing` (exact first line but a trailing diagnostic non-empty line), a header-line-`def greet`-diagnostic stub whose single-line output is `sample.py:1: warning: expected code signature def greet missing` (strict grep-form header with a `def greet`-bearing diagnostic but no argument list), an indented-`def greet`-diagnostic stub whose output is `sample.py:1-6` followed by a two-space-indented `warning: expected code signature def greet missing` (strict range-form header with a `def greet`-bearing indented diagnostic but no argument list), a grep-form header-line-diagnostic stub whose single-line output is `sample.py:1: warning: expected code signature def greet(name): missing` (verbatim full signature embedded as a substring in diagnostic prose — full-line equality rejects it), an indented-diagnostic stub whose output is `sample.py:1-6` followed by a two-space-indented `warning: expected code signature def greet(name): missing` (verbatim full signature embedded as a substring in an indented diagnostic — first-indent full-line equality rejects it), and a non-first-indent-match stub whose output is `sample.py:1-6` followed by a decoy `  warning: no matches` and then an exact `  def greet(name):` later (the one-shot adjacency flag is consumed by the decoy before the real signature ever appears, so the later verbatim line is rejected). Affected: `install.sh`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CLOUD_BOOTSTRAP_PROMPT.md`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/InstallScriptTests.cs`.
- **Record a design decision for the C# reference-extractor ceiling (#384)** — `SELF_IMPROVEMENT.md` now has a dedicated "Design Decision — C# Extraction Ceiling (Issue #384)" section that closes meta-issue #384 with a documented direction: extend the existing hand-written `StructuralLineMasker` into a richer per-line scanner that additionally exposes the enclosing class/method stack, brace/paren/angle-bracket depth, and logical declaration start line, so `SymbolExtractor` / `ReferenceExtractor` regexes can query scope state instead of re-parsing it ad-hoc. Option A (externalizing per-language regex tables into data files) is deferred rather than rejected, because the open C# / Java issues are driven by cross-construct regex interactions, not by language breadth. No dependency-rule exception is needed — the extension stays hand-written like the JS/TS lexer and the existing `StructuralLineMasker`. Explicit exit criteria list which open issues should close or become materially simpler once the scanner exposes scope + declaration-start state: multi-line declarations (#361, #382); string/comment bleed beyond the current masker (#264, #274, #288, #291, #301, #363, #372); nested initializer / bracket tracking (#257, #286, #293, #330); and scope attribution (#233, #242, #252, #316). Issues outside that list stay on the normal per-bug track. The next landing C# / Java reference-extractor fix from that list should be treated as the first real consumer of the extended scanner so the API is shaped by a concrete fix rather than designed in isolation. Affected: `SELF_IMPROVEMENT.md`. Closes #384.
- **T-SQL / SQL Server DDL kinds now surface as symbols (#230)** — The `SymbolExtractor` SQL row previously only captured `CREATE TABLE` / `(MATERIALIZED) VIEW` / `PROCEDURE` / `FUNCTION` / `TRIGGER` / `TYPE` / `SCHEMA` / `SEQUENCE` / `DOMAIN` / `EXTENSION` / `INDEX` and `ALTER TABLE`, so on T-SQL / SQL Server migration scripts the short-form `CREATE PROC`, T-SQL `CREATE OR ALTER` (SQL Server 2016+), `CREATE SYNONYM`, `CREATE DATABASE` / `LOGIN` / `USER` / `ROLE` / `CERTIFICATE`, `CREATE PARTITION FUNCTION` / `PARTITION SCHEME`, `CREATE FULLTEXT CATALOG`, and every non-`TABLE` `ALTER` form (procedures, views, sequences, synonyms, principals, etc.) were silently dropped from the index — making `symbols` / `definition` / `outline` / `inspect` look near-empty on enterprise .NET backends whose primary surface is a stored-procedure or schema-migration repo. The TABLE/VIEW and PROCEDURE/PROC/FUNCTION/TRIGGER rows now accept `CREATE OR (REPLACE|ALTER)`, the procedure row accepts the `PROC` synonym, dedicated rows were added for `CREATE SYNONYM` (class), `CREATE DATABASE|LOGIN|USER|ROLE|CERTIFICATE` (class), `CREATE PARTITION FUNCTION` (function) / `CREATE PARTITION SCHEME` (class), `CREATE FULLTEXT CATALOG` (class), and the `ALTER` side is split into kind-consistent rows so procedure-like `ALTER` (`PROCEDURE` / `PROC` / `FUNCTION` / `TRIGGER` / `PARTITION FUNCTION`) emits kind `function`, `ALTER SCHEMA` emits kind `namespace`, `ALTER EXTENSION` emits kind `import`, and the remaining object kinds (`TABLE`, `(MATERIALIZED) VIEW`, `SEQUENCE`, `SYNONYM`, `LOGIN`, `USER`, `ROLE`, `DATABASE`, `CERTIFICATE`, `INDEX`, `TYPE`, `DOMAIN`, `PARTITION SCHEME`, `FULLTEXT CATALOG`) emit kind `class`. Splitting the `ALTER` row by kind keeps the same object's `CREATE` and `ALTER` symbols under the same `kind` so `symbols --kind function` / `definition` / `inspect` do not duplicate across kinds. The `ALTER` side also now picks up `CERTIFICATE`, `DOMAIN`, and `EXTENSION` that were missing from the original row so every non-`TABLE` `ALTER` form is actually captured rather than just claimed. Every SQL row now shares an identifier shape that accepts PG double-quoted (`"name"`), T-SQL bracketed (`[name]`), or bare (`\w+`) tokens with optional dotted qualifiers such as `[dbo].[sp_X]`, `"schema"."name"`, and `schema.name`. The existing `CREATE INDEX ON tbl` / anonymous-name guard (`(?!ON\b)`), the `CREATE TYPE ... AS ENUM` Postgres branch, and the `CREATE SCHEMA AUTHORIZATION` branch are preserved. Body-less `namespace`-kind symbols from SQL (`CREATE SCHEMA sales;`, `ALTER SCHEMA sales TRANSFER ...;`) would previously trip the `IsFileScopedNamespace` check that wraps every subsequent top-level symbol under a C# `namespace X;` file-scoped declaration — so `ALTER FUNCTION dbo.fn_Total`, `ALTER PARTITION FUNCTION pf_OrdersByYear`, and every later declaration in the same file were emitted with `container_kind='namespace'` / `container_name='sales'`, breaking `definition` / `inspect` / family grouping on real migration scripts. The helper now additionally requires the signature to start with the `namespace` keyword, so SQL schema rows no longer act as file-scoped containers; SQL schema scoping is still expressed through qualified names (`sales.Money`), matching how the rest of cdidx reads SQL. Added a dedicated `Extract_SQL_DetectsTSqlDdlKinds` regression test that locks all thirteen new T-SQL `CREATE` shapes and every new `ALTER` kind contract (`ALTER PROCEDURE` / `ALTER FUNCTION` / `ALTER PARTITION FUNCTION` → `function`; `ALTER SCHEMA` → `namespace`; `ALTER EXTENSION` → `import`; `ALTER CERTIFICATE` / `ALTER DOMAIN` → `class`) including the `CREATE PROC` + `ALTER PROCEDURE` pair that must emit two `dbo.sp_DailyReport` rows both under kind `function`, and asserts that no later top-level SQL symbol is wrapped under `namespace=sales` so the file-scoped-namespace container pollution cannot regress. `GO` batch boundary awareness and `BEGIN ... END` structural nesting are deliberately out of scope here and remain filed in #230 as stretch items. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #230.
- **Oracle PL/SQL DDL kinds and `.pks` / `.pkb` / `.pls` / `.plb` extensions now surface as symbols (#231)** — `FileIndexer.LangMap` only routed `.sql` and `.plsql` to the `sql` language, so Oracle source trees that split packages into `*.pks` (package spec), `*.pkb` (package body), `*.pls` (PL/SQL script), and `*.plb` (wrapped PL/SQL) were silently skipped by `ScanFilesDetailed` / `BuildRecord` and never reached `cdidx search` / `files` / `outline` / `map` / `symbols`. Even on files that were indexed as `sql`, the `SymbolExtractor` SQL rows never matched `CREATE [OR REPLACE] PACKAGE [BODY] <name>`, `CREATE [OR REPLACE] TYPE BODY <name>`, `CREATE [SHARED] [PUBLIC] DATABASE LINK <name>`, or Oracle-only `CREATE DIRECTORY` / `CREATE CONTEXT` / `CREATE PROFILE`, and the bare-identifier class `\w+` rejected Oracle-legal `$` / `#` characters that routinely appear in system names like `SYS$LINK` / `USER#1`. Added the four Oracle file extensions to `LangMap`; widened every SQL identifier token (bare, bracketed, double-quoted, dotted qualifiers) to `[\w$#]+` uniformly across every SQL row so cross-dialect consistency is preserved; added dedicated rows for `CREATE [OR REPLACE] [EDITIONABLE|NONEDITIONABLE] PACKAGE [BODY] <name>`, `CREATE [OR REPLACE] TYPE BODY <name>`, `CREATE [SHARED] [PUBLIC] DATABASE LINK <name>` (accepting the full Oracle modifier grid including the 2-word `SHARED PUBLIC` form), and `CREATE [OR REPLACE] (DIRECTORY|CONTEXT|PROFILE) <name>` (all kind `class`); and extended `CREATE SYNONYM` to accept `OR REPLACE` and an optional `PUBLIC` qualifier. Regex ordering matters — the new `PACKAGE BODY` row precedes the bare `PACKAGE` row, `TYPE BODY` precedes the bare `TYPE` row, and `DATABASE LINK` precedes the bare `DATABASE` row, so the trailing keywords `BODY` / `LINK` are never misread as the object name. On the `ALTER` side, only `ALTER DATABASE LINK <name>` needs a dedicated row (it must precede the bare `ALTER DATABASE` row so `LINK` is not absorbed as the object name); Oracle's real body-compile syntax is `ALTER PACKAGE <name> COMPILE BODY` / `ALTER TYPE <name> COMPILE BODY` (the keyword `BODY` appears *after* the object name, not before it), so `PACKAGE` is added to the generic `ALTER` kind-list and both forms fall through to that row naturally — no separate `ALTER PACKAGE BODY <name>` / `ALTER TYPE BODY <name>` rows are introduced, because those keyword orderings are not valid Oracle SQL. `DIRECTORY` / `PROFILE` are also added to the generic `ALTER` kind-list so they emit as `class`. Added a dedicated `Extract_SQL_DetectsOraclePlSqlDdlKinds` regression test that locks all eight new `CREATE` shapes (including `SYS$ITEMS#1` for the `$` / `#` identifier acceptance), the real-syntax `ALTER` forms (`ALTER PACKAGE <name> COMPILE [BODY]`, `ALTER TYPE <name> COMPILE BODY`, `ALTER DATABASE LINK`, `ALTER DIRECTORY`, `ALTER PROFILE`), and explicit negative assertions that `BODY` and `LINK` are never captured as the object name on the `CREATE` side. Added four `FileIndexerTests` `[InlineData]` cases pinning that `orders_pkg.pls`, `orders_pkg.pks`, `orders_pkg.pkb`, and `orders_pkg.plb` all route to the `sql` language. Oracle `q'[ ... ]'` alternative-quoted string literals and anonymous PL/SQL blocks are intentionally out of scope (tracked in #177). Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #231.

#### Fixed
- **C# `partial` indexers and `partial` events are no longer dropped from symbol extraction (#350)** — When #332 added `partial` to the C# property regex, #355 added the inheritance modifiers (`virtual` / `override` / `abstract` / `sealed` / `new`) to the event regex, and the method regex already covered `partial`, the indexer and event rows were left out of the `partial` modifier expansion. As a result every C# 13 `partial int this[int i] { get; }` / `partial string this[string key] { get => ... }` indexer declaration and every C# 14 field-like or accessor-based `partial event System.Action X` / `partial event System.Action<string> OnLog { add { ... } remove { ... } }` declaration produced zero symbol rows — `cdidx symbols`, `definition`, `outline`, and `inspect` silently reported an empty indexer / event surface on any partial type that moved those members across declaration / implementation partials, even though the exact same shapes without `partial` (and the exact same `partial` shapes on methods / properties) were captured normally. Added `partial` to the modifier lookahead of both the indexer and event rows in `SymbolExtractor`, keeping the rest of each regex unchanged so the existing `visibility` / `returnType` / `Signature` / `Name=="Item"` contracts hold. Added `Extract_CSharp_DetectsPartialIndexers` and `Extract_CSharp_DetectsPartialEvents` regression tests that pin declaration + implementation pairs across two partial class fragments (expression-body and block-body indexer shapes, field-like and accessor-based event shapes, both emit under the expected kind with `public` visibility and `partial` preserved in the recovered signature) while the non-partial baseline indexer and non-partial baseline event continue to extract as before. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #350.
- **C# properties whose first accessor carries its own visibility modifier are locked in as captured (#332)** — `public int X { internal get; set; }`, `{ private get; public set; }`, `{ protected internal get; set; }`, and `{ private protected get; set; }` were reported missing from the symbol index in v1.10.0. The current extractor already handles them through `HasCSharpPropertyAccessorStart` + `TrySkipCSharpAccessorAccessibility`, which tolerate accessor-level attributes and one- or two-word accessibility modifiers before the first accessor keyword, but there was no dedicated regression pinning the behavior. Added a `SymbolExtractor` regression test that asserts all four first-accessor-visibility shapes plus the standard second-accessor variants appear as `property` symbols and none of them leak as phantom `function` rows. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`.
- **Query CLI no longer swallows a neighboring flag when a value-taking option is followed by another recognized option (#184)** — `QueryCommandRunner.ParseArgs` now treats any recognized CLI option (e.g. `--json`, `--limit`, `--lang`) in the next-arg slot as a missing-value error for the current option, instead of consuming it as the value and silently dropping it. Previously `cdidx search hello --limit --lang rust` parsed `--lang` as the `--limit` value, failed numeric validation with a confusing "got '--lang'" message, and dropped the actual `--lang rust` pair entirely. The new `IsRecognizedOptionToken` guard fires inside `TryReadRawOptionValue` (numeric options) unconditionally, and inside `TryReadStringOptionValue` only when the option does NOT accept separated dash-prefixed literal values, so the error now reports "`--limit requires a value`" cleanly. Options that legitimately accept dashed literals (`--db`, `--path`, `--exclude-path`, `--query`) intentionally bypass the guard so the pre-existing contract is preserved: `--db --json` / `--path --json` / `--exclude-path --json` still fail closed with the inline-form hint (`pass it as \`--db=<value>\``), and `--query --json` still accepts `--json` as literal query text — use `--query=<value>` to disambiguate if a flag name collides with a literal query. Non-repeatable value-taking options (`--db`, `--limit` / `--top`, `--lang`, `--query`, `--kind`, `--since`, `--start`, `--end`, `--before`, `--after`, `--focus-line`, `--focus-column`, `--focus-length`, `--snippet-lines`, `--max-line-width`, `--depth`) now also emit a `Warning: <option> specified more than once; using the last value '<v>'.` on every repeat so scripted or copy-pasted duplicates are visible instead of silent take-last; `--top` is canonicalized to `--limit` so `--limit 5 --top 10` also warns. Repeatable options (`--path`, `--exclude-path`, `--name`) are deliberately excluded. Added regression locks for each missing-value and duplicate-warning path, for dashed-literal preservation (`--db` / `--path` / `--exclude-path`) and `--query` dashed-literal acceptance, and for positive-integer validation of `--focus-column` / `--max-line-width` (zero and non-numeric must fail closed). Pre-existing missing-value tests were updated to reflect the earlier short-circuit ("requires a value" now replaces the downstream "requires a positive integer" for recognized-flag-as-value cases). Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`.
- **C# properties whose first accessor carries its own visibility modifier are locked in as captured (#332)** — `public int X { internal get; set; }`, `{ private get; public set; }`, `{ protected internal get; set; }`, and `{ private protected get; set; }` were reported missing from the symbol index in v1.10.0. The current extractor already handles them through `HasCSharpPropertyAccessorStart` + `TrySkipCSharpAccessorAccessibility`, which tolerate accessor-level attributes and one- or two-word accessibility modifiers before the first accessor keyword, but there was no dedicated regression pinning the behavior. Added a `SymbolExtractor` regression test that asserts all four first-accessor-visibility shapes plus the standard second-accessor variants appear as `property` symbols and none of them leak as phantom `function` rows. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`.
- **JavaScript / TypeScript optional chaining calls (`foo?.()`) are now captured as `call` references (#294)** — `ReferenceExtractor.CallRegex` required the captured identifier to be followed directly by `\s*\(` (with optional generic arguments in between), so a JS / TS optional chaining call such as `callback?.()`, `onSuccess?.(data)`, or the `handler?.()` tail of `obj?.handler?.()` — where the `?.` sits between the identifier and the argument-list `(` — never matched and the `call` edge to `callback` / `onSuccess` / `handler` silently disappeared from `references`, `callers`, `callees`, `inspect`, and `impact`. The regex now accepts an optional `?.` segment immediately after the captured name, followed by the existing optional generic argument list (fixed order: `name` → optional `?.` → optional `<...>` → `(`), so both bare optional chaining calls (`callback?.()`) and TypeScript's explicit-type-argument variant (`callback?.<T>()`) are captured. Other supported languages that use `?.` for null-conditional / safe-call (`C#`, `Kotlin`, `Swift`, `Dart`) always place an identifier between `?.` and `(`, so their existing call sites continue to match via the trailing identifier and are unaffected. Added `Extract_JsOptionalChainingCall_CapturesCallReference` and `Extract_TsOptionalChainingCallWithTypeArgs_CapturesCallReference` regressions covering the bare, argumented, property-chained-optional-call, and type-argument forms; the chained-optional-call case (`obj?.handler?.()`) is deliberately chosen because on `main` the old `CallRegex` does not match `handler` (the `?.` between `handler` and `(` blocks the match), so the test actually fails without the `(?:\?\.)?` addition. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #294.
- **C# / Java parenless object / collection / dictionary / array initializers are now recorded as `instantiate` (#286)** — `ReferenceExtractor` previously required a trailing `(` (via `CallRegex` + `IsConstructorCallName`) to upgrade a `new <Type>` site to `instantiate`, so the parenless C# object initializer (`new Foo { X = 1 }`), collection initializer (`new List<int> { 1, 2, 3 }`), dictionary initializer (`new Dictionary<string, int> { ["k"] = 1 }`), and C# / Java array initializer (`new Bar[] { ... }`, `new String[] { "a", "b" }`) shapes were silently dropped from `references` / `callers` / `impact` / `inspect`, even though the type is genuinely instantiated. A new compiled regex `CSharpJavaInitializerRegex` runs before the shared `CallRegex` loop and matches `new <name>` followed by an optional one-level generic argument list, zero or more array dimension specifiers (so jagged `[][]`, multi-dimensional `[,]`, and sized `[N]` shapes are covered), and a literal `{`. A companion `CSharpJavaInitializerTrailingRegex` handles the Allman-style multi-line form where `new <Type>` ends the current line and `{` sits on the next non-blank line (e.g. `new Bag\n{\n    Items = ...\n}`): it anchors on end-of-line and the extractor peeks forward to the next non-blank prepared line to confirm it begins with `{` before emitting an `instantiate` edge, so trailing `new Foo\n;` or `new Foo\n(1, 2);` shapes do not produce phantom rows. Qualified type names (`new N.Foo { ... }`, `new global::N.Foo { ... }`) walk the leading `name (.|::)` segments so the trailing identifier is captured exactly like the existing `CallRegex` + `IsConstructorCallName` path captures `new N.Foo()`. The pass is gated to `csharp` / `java` only and intentionally does not match anonymous types (`new { Name = ... }`), target-typed `new()`, or collection expressions (`new[] { ... }`) because they have no named target. C# built-in type aliases (`int`, `string`, `void`, `dynamic`, `var`, ...) and Java primitive type names (`int`, `boolean`, `void`, ...) are skipped via the existing `CSharpBuiltInTypeNames` / `JavaPrimitiveTypeNames` filters so `new int[] { 1, 2, 3 }` does not produce a phantom `instantiate int` row, and the same `IsIgnoredCallName` / `definitionNames` / `ResolveContainerForCall` post-filters apply so attribution lands on the correct innermost container (function / property / record primary constructor / Java same-line ctor synthesis). The new pattern intentionally does not match `new Foo() { X = 1 }` because the `(` then `)` then `{` shape forces the existing `CallRegex` + `IsConstructorCallName` path to fire instead — same edge, no double emission. Nested generics deeper than one `<...>` level (`new Dictionary<string, List<int>> { ... }`) still hit the same regex limitation as the existing `CallRegex` generics handling and remain a separate follow-up. Added `Extract_CsharpParenlessInitializers_AreInstantiate` (object / collection / dictionary / `new int[]` skip / `new Bar[] { new Bar() { X = 9 } }` outer + inner / negative `if (true) { }` guard / no double `call` for any of `Bar` / `List` / `Dictionary`), `Extract_CsharpQualifiedParenlessInitializer_IsInstantiate` (`new N.Foo { ... }` and `new global::N.Bar { ... }`), `Extract_JavaParenlessArrayInitializer_IsInstantiate` (`new String[] { "a", "b" }` captured + `int` / `boolean` skipped), and `Extract_CsharpAllmanParenlessInitializers_AreInstantiate` which pins the multi-line form (`new Bag\n{...}`, `new List<Foo>\n{...}`, `new Foo\n{...}`, `new Foo[]\n{...}`) and a negative case (`new Foo\n;`) so the trailing-regex path cannot regress into phantom `instantiate` emission when no `{` actually follows. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #286.
- **SQL `CREATE` / `ALTER PROCEDURE` / `PROC` / `FUNCTION` / `TRIGGER` bodies now carry body ranges, so calls inside the body attribute to the enclosing proc (#429)** — `SymbolExtractor` emitted every `CREATE` / `ALTER PROCEDURE` / `PROC` / `FUNCTION` / `TRIGGER` with `BodyStyle.None`, leaving `BodyStartLine` / `BodyEndLine` null. `ReferenceExtractor.ResolveContainerForCall` → `FindInnermostContainer` relies on those ranges to attribute an in-body call to the enclosing procedure, so every call inside a procedure body fell through to the file-level fallback and `symbol_references.container_kind` / `container_name` were written as null. As a result `cdidx callers` / `callees` / `impact` returned zero for every SQL procedure even though `graph_supported` reported true. The procedure/function/trigger rows now emit a new `BodyStyle.SqlProcBody`, and the new `FindSqlProcBodyRange(lines, startIndex)` helper scans forward for (1) a balanced PostgreSQL dollar-quoted body (`$$ ... $$` / `$tag$ ... $tag$`) when the next non-blank payload begins with a dollar tag, (2) a T-SQL `GO` batch separator at line start (trailing `;` / `--` comment tolerated), (3) a sibling proc-like DDL start (`CREATE` / `ALTER` / `DROP` + optional `OR REPLACE` or `OR ALTER` + `PROCEDURE` / `PROC` / `FUNCTION` / `TRIGGER`) — narrowed from the original `CREATE|ALTER|DROP|GRANT|REVOKE|DENY|USE` catch-all so body-internal `CREATE TABLE #tmp` / `ALTER TABLE` / `GRANT` / `USE` do not prematurely close the proc body and re-introduce issue #429, and the `OR REPLACE` / `OR ALTER` alternation is kept in sync with the CREATE-side symbol regex so a T-SQL `CREATE OR ALTER PROCEDURE` sibling (SQL Server 2016+) without an intervening `GO` actually terminates the previous body range, or (4) end-of-file. Before scanning each line, `MaskSqlLineForBodyScan` strips `--` line comments, `/* ... */` block comments (including PostgreSQL-style nested `/* /* ... */ ... */` via a `blockCommentDepth` counter threaded across lines via `ref int` — depth increments on every `/*` and decrements on every `*/`, so the inner `*/` no longer exits the outer comment and re-exposes `GO` / `CREATE PROCEDURE` tokens; T-SQL / MySQL / Oracle do not support nested block comments but the depth counter is strictly safer for those dialects too because a non-nested outer `*/` still closes when depth returns to 0), and `'..'` / `".."` string literals (preserving column width so later column alignment stays correct, and preserving `[name]` / `` `name` `` quoted identifiers because SQL quoted identifiers are not string literals) so a `GO` / `$$` / `CREATE PROCEDURE` token embedded in a string or comment does not close the body early. Both the `GO` terminator and the sibling-proc-DDL terminator are evaluated against the masked text for the same reason. `ALTER PARTITION FUNCTION` is intentionally split into its own pattern and keeps `BodyStyle.None` because it modifies a partition boundary value rather than executable code, so its surface should remain body-less. Added twelve `SymbolExtractor` regression tests covering T-SQL `BEGIN ... END` bodies terminated by `GO`, Postgres dollar-quoted function bodies, single-line `AS BEGIN ... END;` bodies, DDL-start close without an intervening `GO`, string / comment masking (a `GO` / `$$` / new proc-like `CREATE` inside a string literal or `--` comment does not close the body), `ALTER PROCEDURE` body capture, `ALTER PARTITION FUNCTION` staying body-less, a regression guard that a second procedure is not swallowed into the previous procedure's body range, body-internal `CREATE TABLE #tmp` / `ALTER TABLE` not closing the body, a multi-line `/* ... */` block containing bare `GO` / fake `CREATE PROCEDURE` headers not closing the body, a T-SQL `CREATE OR ALTER PROCEDURE` sibling without an intervening `GO` closing the prior body, and a nested `/* /* GO CREATE PROCEDURE ... */ GO CREATE PROCEDURE ... */` block comment that must not exit on the inner `*/`. Added two `ReferenceExtractor` regression tests: `Extract_SqlCallInsideProcedureBody_AttributesCallerToEnclosingProcedure` pins that an `EXEC` inside a T-SQL `CREATE PROCEDURE dbo.sp_Outer` body resolves to `ContainerKind=function` / `ContainerName=dbo.sp_Outer` (schema-qualified, matching the persisted `SymbolRecord.Name`) while a post-`GO` call has null container, and `Extract_SqlPostgresDollarQuotedBody_AttributesCallerToEnclosingFunction` pins the same for a `PERFORM public.fn_inner()` inside a Postgres `$$ ... $$`-quoted `public.fn_outer` body. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #429.
- **C# 11 `static abstract` / `abstract static` interface operator members are no longer dropped from symbol extraction (#244)** — The `SymbolExtractor` conversion (`implicit` / `explicit`) and binary/unary operator rows for C# accepted only `static|unsafe|extern` in their modifier slot (and the same narrow set in the leading `(?=...static\s+)` lookahead), so a C# 11 interface declaring `static abstract T operator +(T a, T b);` / `abstract static T operator -(T a, T b);` / `static abstract implicit operator T(int x);` silently produced zero rows on both modifier orders, while the identical `public static T operator +(...)` declarations on a class or struct were captured as normal. That regressed every generic-math interface in `System.Numerics` (`INumber<TSelf>`, `IAdditionOperators`, `ISubtractionOperators`, `IMultiplyOperators`, `IDivisionOperators`, `IComparisonOperators`, `IEqualityOperators`, `IBitwiseOperators`, `IIncrementOperators`, `IUnaryNegationOperators`, `IBinaryInteger`, etc.) and any user-defined interface whose arithmetic contract relies on `static abstract` operators — `cdidx definition "+"` / `callers` / `references` / `outline` / `inspect` reported zero operator hits on the interface side, so AI clients browsing a generic-math API saw only `Zero` / `Compare` and never the arithmetic surface the interface actually defines. The regex modifier slot on both operator rows (and the matching lookahead anchor) now also accepts `abstract|virtual|sealed|override|new`, so both modifier orders and both operator families are captured the same way the method regex (which already allowed this modifier slot) captures `abstract static int Compare(T a, T b);`. Scope is kept deliberately narrow: this fix only teaches the two operator rows the modifiers that are legal on a C# 11 `static abstract` / `abstract static` interface operator. As a side effect the existing operator-name group — which already accepts `operator checked +` / `operator checked -` / `explicit operator checked int` — now also covers the user-defined checked-operator variants on those same `static abstract` / `abstract static` interfaces, because widening the modifier slot is what was blocking them. Broader `operator checked` follow-up work outside this modifier slot remains tracked separately in #238. Added `Extract_CSharp_DetectsStaticAbstractInterfaceOperators` which runs the issue #244 fixture end-to-end (interface with `static abstract T operator +`, `abstract static T operator -`, `static abstract T operator *`, `static abstract implicit operator T(int x)`, `abstract static explicit operator int(T t)`, plus the baseline `Zero` property and `Compare` method, `static abstract T operator checked +(T a, T b)` and `abstract static explicit operator checked int(T t)` pinning the incidental `operator checked` coverage, alongside a sibling struct carrying `public static N operator +`/`-` so the pre-existing struct-level capture is not regressed) and pins that every operator row — including both modifier orders and both conversion and regular operators, with and without `checked` — is emitted with `Kind == "function"` and the expected operator name. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #244.
- **`cdidx unused` no longer loses reflection context across multi-line attribute literals (#409)** — Closing #375 taught the `unused` reflection-attribute scanner to treat `[` / `]` inside a single-line attribute string argument as literal text rather than bracket depth, but the guard was purely per-line. When a C# attribute straddles multiple physical lines via a verbatim (`@"..."`), raw (`"""..."""`), or raw-interpolated (`$"""..."""` / `$$"""..."""`) string literal whose body contains `[` or `]` — e.g. `[JsonPropertyName(@"a[\n]")]\npublic string A { get; set; }` or the same attribute inline-closed on the declaration line (`[JsonPropertyName(@"a[\n]")] public string A ...`) — the continuation row landed in `GetAdjacentAttributeBlock` as a bare `]")]` (or `]")] public string A ...`). `LineContainsInlineAttributeAndDeclaration` only anchors on a leading `[`, so the guard did not fire and the walker either (a) dropped the real `[JsonPropertyName(...)]` block and let the reflection attribute fall off `A`, or (b) let that attribute leak down onto an unrelated property `B` below. The reader now threads C# lexer state across the whole excerpt via a new `SymbolExtractor.SanitizeCSharpLinesForCrossLineScan` helper that reuses the existing `LexCSharpLine` state machine (including raw-interpolated `$` prefix / quote-run tracking from #375) and additionally blanks string / char delimiters (`"`, `'`, `\`) so a continuation row does not look like it opens a fresh string literal when walked in isolation. `GetAdjacentAttributeBlock` consumes both the original and sanitized lines: it keeps declaration / bracket-depth logic on the original line where needed, and uses a new `SanitizedLineHasInlineDeclarationTail` predicate (non-whitespace content after the last `]` on the sanitized line) both as a fast-path on the anchor line (so `]")] public string A ...` is recognized as "declaration lives on this row, don't walk forward to pick up `B`") and as an additional trigger for the existing #375 inline-decl guard (so the attribute does not leak onto the next plain property). Added a `GetUnusedSymbols_MultilineAttributeLiteralWithBracketInString_KeepsReflectionContext` `[Theory]` covering all 7 shapes (verbatim / raw / `$` raw-interpolated / `$$` raw-interpolated, both standalone-declaration and inline-closed-on-declaration variants), pinning that `A` stays `reflection_or_config_suspect` while the adjacent plain `B` stays `public_or_exported_no_refs`. The same fix also covers two related leaks the dogfooding review caught: (1) `[JsonPropertyName("ok")] // trailing comment\npublic string C ...` used to fall back to `public_or_exported_no_refs` because `StripLeadingCSharpAttributeLists` left the `// comment` tail in place, which the inline-declaration guard treated as a real declaration body. The guard now runs against the sanitized line for both the leading-`[` inline-decl check and the multi-line tail check, so blanked comments no longer impersonate declaration content. (2) `[JsonPropertyName("ok")] /* trailing block comment */\npublic string D ...` had two independent failure modes on the same row: `BuildTriviaMask` flagged any line containing `*/` as trivia, so `FindPreviousNonTriviaLine` overshot past the real attribute row, AND `BuildSingleLineTrivia` (used by `ExtractNormalizedAttributeNames` to filter comment rows out of the captured block) likewise discarded the whole line once it contained `*/`, so even when the block walker did reach the row, the attribute name `JsonPropertyName` never made it into the candidate set. `BuildTriviaMask` now derives triviality from the cross-line-sanitized form (a line is trivia iff its sanitized version is all whitespace — strings / chars / `//` / `/* ... */` with state carried across physical lines are all blanked) and `BuildSingleLineTrivia` no longer treats mid-line `*/` as pure trivia (the lone `*/` closing row is still caught by the existing `StartsWith('*')` check). (3) A multi-line block comment embedded inside an attribute list — e.g. `[\n    /* explanation\n       [JsonIgnore] */\n    JsonPropertyName("ok")\n]\npublic string E ...` — still leaked a phantom `JsonIgnore` into the attribute-name set because the comment-closing row `[JsonIgnore] */` survived `BuildSingleLineTrivia` as real text and `ExtractNormalizedAttributeNames` parsed it as a real attribute row, which then cancelled the real `JsonPropertyName` via the `ReflectionIgnoreAttributeNames` set. `GetAdjacentAttributeBlock` now builds the returned attribute block from the cross-line-sanitized lines (not the originals), so the comment body — including any bracketed identifier inside it — is already blanked when it reaches the attribute-name parser, and `ExtractNormalizedAttributeNames` never sees the phantom row. The same switch to sanitized lines also hardens the inline `[attr] decl` anchor path against single-line block comments wrapped around bracketed text. (4) The cross-line sanitizer's verbatim and raw-string handlers still did not understand interpolation holes, so `[JsonPropertyName($@"{\n"[JsonIgnore]"}")]\npublic string A ...` — and the equivalent `@$"..."` / `$"""..."""` forms — let an inner `"` (or inner `"""` quote run) inside the hole prematurely close the outer interpolated string. After that premature close, the continuation line `"[JsonIgnore]"}")]` was lexed as fresh code, and `[JsonIgnore]` was picked up as a real attribute name that cancelled the real `[JsonPropertyName]` via the `ReflectionIgnoreAttributeNames` set. `CSharpLexState` now also tracks `IsInterpolated`, `InterpolationDollarCount`, `InterpolationBraceDepth`, and `InterpolationReturnMode` / `InterpolationReturnRawDelimiterLength` / `InterpolationReturnDollarCount` so the sanitizer can enter an interpolation hole on the matching `{` run (single `{` for `$@"..."` / `@$"..."`, N consecutive `{` matching the outer `$` prefix length for raw-interpolated strings), track brace depth inside the hole while in `Code` mode, and return to the outer `VerbatimString` / `RawString` mode only when the matching `}` (or `}` run for raw-interpolated) is seen. This mirrors the single-line `TrySkipCSharpStringOrCharLiteral` approximation already used elsewhere in the reader: one level of nesting is sufficient to cover the reflection-attribute scan, and nested interpolation inside a hole is still approximated rather than fully modeled. The `{{` / `}}` literal escapes inside verbatim-interpolated strings are also handled so escaped braces do not open or close a hole. Three new `[InlineData]` rows pin this on the existing `GetUnusedSymbols_MultilineAttributeLiteralWithBracketInString_KeepsReflectionContext` theory: `verbatim_interp_hole_with_dollar_at` (`$@"..."`), `verbatim_interp_hole_with_at_dollar` (`@$"..."`), and `raw_interp_hole_with_triple_quote_run` (`$"""..."""` with an inner `"""[JsonIgnore]"""` quote run in the hole). (5) The inline `[attr] decl;` anchor used by `GetAdjacentAttributeBlock` still consulted the original anchor line instead of the sanitized one, so a valid C# shape where a block comment sits on the same row as an inline attribute and its declaration — e.g. `/* note */ [JsonPropertyName("ok")] public string A { get; set; } = "";` — failed the leading-`[` anchor and fell back to upward search, which emptied the attribute block and flipped `A` out of `reflection_or_config_suspect` into `public_or_exported_no_refs`.
