The anchor now runs `LineContainsInlineAttributeAndDeclaration` against the sanitized line, which the cross-line sanitizer has already blanked into `           [JsonPropertyName(    )] public string A ...`, so the leading-`[` anchor is satisfied. The #409 intent of not treating multi-line literal continuation tails like `]")] public string A ...` as inline declarations is preserved: sanitization cannot turn a continuation-leading `)` into a `[`, so such rows still fall through to the bracket-boundary path. Pinned by `GetUnusedSymbols_CommentPrefixedInlineAttribute_KeepsReflectionContext`, `GetUnusedSymbols_AttributeLineWithTrailingLineComment_KeepsReflectionContext`, `GetUnusedSymbols_AttributeLineWithTrailingBlockComment_KeepsReflectionContext`, and `GetUnusedSymbols_MultilineAttributeWithEmbeddedBlockCommentMentioningIgnoreAttribute_KeepsReflectionContext`. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`. Closes #409.
- **HTML `.htm` / `.xhtml` / `.shtml` were silently skipped, and `.html` indexed text but extracted zero symbols (#215)** — `FileIndexer.LangMap` only listed `.html` for the `html` language, so sibling extensions `.htm` (legacy / Windows / IIS default), `.xhtml` (XHTML), and `.shtml` (server-side includes) returned `null` from language detection and were skipped entirely by `ScanFilesDetailed` / `BuildRecord`, never reaching `cdidx search` / `files` / `outline` / `map` / `definition`. `.html` files themselves were picked up as raw text (chunks + FTS5) but `SymbolExtractor.PatternCache` had no `"html"` entry, so every `html` file produced zero `symbols` / `definition` / `references` / `inspect` rows — `cdidx languages` showed `html` with `Symbols: -` — even when the source contained landmark IDs (`<header id="main-header">`), inline anchor targets, external `<script src="...">` / `<link href="...">` that JS files depend on, or custom Web Component tags. Added `.htm`, `.xhtml`, and `.shtml` to `LangMap` so they route to the `html` language on scan and indexing. HTML symbol extraction is implemented as a dedicated character-level state machine in `ExtractHtmlSymbols` instead of the generic regex pattern loop, because line-oriented regex (even with quoted-attribute masks) cannot safely distinguish real attributes from attribute-lookalike strings inside quoted values, multi-line quoted values, raw-text bodies, or comments — earlier regex iterations of this fix repeatedly leaked phantom symbols (or dropped real ones) on same-tag attribute lookalikes like `<link title="href=evil.css" href="/real.css">`, on quoted `>` characters inside opening tags like `<script data-note="a > b" src="/app.js">`, and on reserved SVG/MathML hyphenated tags like `<font-face>` / `<annotation-xml>`. The state machine walks tag openers, reads attribute names and both quoted and unquoted attribute values (HTML5 permits unquoted shapes like `<section id=real>`, `<script src=/app.js>`, `<link rel=stylesheet href=/app.css>`), and emits: (1) external `<script src="...">` and `<link href="...">` values as kind `import` (so referenced JS / CSS / icon / preload targets are navigable; inline `<script>` without `src` emits no phantom import); (2) `id="..."` / `id='...'` / unquoted `id=...` attribute values as kind `property`, structurally ignoring `data-id=` / `aria-*id=` / `xml:id=` and bare `id="..."` appearing inside body prose; (3) hyphenated custom Web Component opening tag names (`<my-button>`, `<app-sidebar>`) as kind `class`, skipping the eight reserved SVG/MathML hyphenated tags tracked in `HtmlReservedHyphenatedTags` (`annotation-xml`, `color-profile`, `font-face`, `font-face-src`, `font-face-uri`, `font-face-format`, `font-face-name`, `missing-glyph`). A companion `MaskHtmlRawTextRegions` — also rewritten from regex to a character state machine — blanks the body (but not the opening tag) of `<script>` / `<style>` / `<textarea>` / `<title>` raw-text / RCDATA elements and the contents of `<!-- ... -->` comments before attribute extraction runs, preserving newlines so 1-based line numbers reported by `FindHtmlLineNumber` via a precomputed `lineStarts[]` binary search stay aligned with the raw source. For mid-edit working trees the state machine is deliberately resilient: `FindHtmlQuoteClose` is shared between the masker and the attribute parser so both agree on quote termination — it allows valid multi-line quoted values (e.g. a `title="line1\nline2"` attribute followed by a real `id="real"` later on the same line) and tag-like content inside quoted values (`<div title="line1\n<section></section>\nline3" id="real">` still emits `id="real"` and does NOT leak the embedded `<section id=phantom>` as a phantom `property`), identifying the closing quote via post-value context — a quote is accepted as the close only when the next character is `>`, whitespace, or EOF, plus the XHTML self-closing marker `"/>` (bare `/` is intentionally excluded because it is ambiguous between a self-closing marker and the opening quote of a later path-like attribute such as `href="/app.css"`, which would otherwise let an earlier unterminated `title="...` silently steal it and swallow every sibling tag between them; the `"/>` form is unambiguous because the `/` is followed by `>` so void-element tags like `<link href="/app.css"/>` still close cleanly without triggering the nested fallback on the following sibling) — and non-strong quote candidates that look like a nested attribute opening (`[attr-name-chars]+=` preceded by whitespace) are treated as nested attribute starts and walked past so strict-HTML5 multi-line values still close at their real `>`, while truly unterminated outer quotes bail at the current line so the attribute parser can resume at the next `<` instead of walking to EOF. `MaskHtmlRawTextRegions` also walks past non-raw-text tag openers (`<div`, `<section>`, `</div>`, etc.) using `FindHtmlTagOpenerEnd` so `<script>` / `<style>` / `<textarea>` / `<title>` or `<!--` appearing inside another tag's quoted attribute value (`<div title="<script>">` / `<div title="<!--">`) stays part of the attribute value and is not re-interpreted as a raw-text opener or comment opener on the next character — without that skip, the earlier char-by-char mask scan would re-enter the raw-text / comment branch and mask through EOF, silently dropping every sibling tag after the outer tag. If the outer non-raw-text tag is itself mid-edit and never closes (no matching `"` before EOF), the mask pass advances past the current line instead of falling back to a single-char step, so a `<!--` / `<script>` sitting inside the broken quoted value is still not re-encountered as a real comment / raw-text opener on the very next character — sibling tags on later lines survive. `<![CDATA[...]]>` sections (valid in XHTML / inline SVG / MathML), processing instructions `<?...?>`, and `<!DOCTYPE...>` declarations are also masked in `MaskHtmlRawTextRegions` using their real terminators (`]]>`, `?>`, and a quote-aware `>` walk respectively) so markup-like text inside them does not leak as phantom symbols — a naive "first `>`" scan would stop early inside CDATA containing `<two-widget>` content and let the remainder be parsed as real HTML. An unterminated raw-text opener still masks from `<` to EOF (spec-correct) instead of leaking script-body content as attribute symbols. Cross-line opening tags still emit imports with their `Line` / `StartLine` anchored to the line that actually carries the `src=` / `href=` attribute value rather than the `<` opening line. Added thirteen `SymbolExtractorTests` regressions covering: quoted and unquoted `id` attributes plus negative tests pinning that `data-id` / `aria-hiddenid` / `xml:id` / body-prose `id="..."` do not produce phantom symbols; external `<script src>` / `<link href>` as imports plus confirmation that inline `<script>` without `src` emits no phantom import; hyphenated custom elements as classes with confirmation that `<div>` is not captured; minified multi-tag lines emitting one symbol per match; single-line and multi-line `<!-- ... -->` comments not leaking imports / classes / properties; `<script>` / `<style>` raw-text bodies not leaking symbols from template strings or `url()` arguments; `<script src="...">` still emitting its import when the script element carries raw-text children; multi-line `<script type="module" src="/app.js">` and `<link rel="stylesheet" href="/app.css">` opening tags still emitting their imports on the attribute-value line; `<textarea>` / `<title>` RCDATA bodies not leaking phantom custom-element classes or `id` properties while a real sibling `<section id="real">` is still captured; unclosed `<script>` / `<style>` / `<textarea>` / `<title>` and unclosed `<!--` not cascading phantom symbols; quoted `>` characters inside raw-text opening tags preserving following sibling symbols; reserved SVG/MathML hyphenated tags producing zero class symbols while `<my-widget>` and `<app-sidebar>` are still captured; same-tag attribute lookalikes like `<link title="href=evil.css" href="/real.css">` still emitting the real `/real.css` import; multi-line valid quoted attribute values not breaking following attributes; and an unterminated quote inside a raw-text opener not leaking script-body content as phantom symbols. Added four `FileIndexerTests` `[InlineData]` cases pinning that `index.html`, `legacy.htm`, `doc.xhtml`, and `page.shtml` all route to the `html` language. Updated the `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md` language-pattern reference table with a dedicated `HTML` row (document count bumped from 32 to 33, and HTML removed from the `indexed as raw text without symbol extraction` list so the count there drops from 14 to 13); `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md` and `CLAUDE.md` now document the HTML state-machine dispatch alongside the existing JS/TS state-machine exception. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`, `CLAUDE.md`. Closes #215.
- **C# constructors with a wrapped leading modifier are no longer dropped from symbol extraction (#348)** — `SymbolExtractor`'s C# constructor and static-constructor rows matched the declaration on a single physical line, so wrapped declarations where the leading modifier (`static` / `public` / `private` / `protected` / `internal` / `unsafe` / `extern`) sits on its own line and the `Name(...)` header sits on the next line — e.g. `static\nA() { ... }` or `public\nB() { ... }` — silently fell through the regex and were not emitted as `function` symbols at all. `definition`, `symbols`, `outline`, `inspect`, `callers`, `callees`, and `impact` therefore reported zero rows for the affected constructors on codebases whose formatter wraps long attribute + modifier + ctor headers onto separate lines (a common shape after `[System.Obsolete]` / `[Conditional(...)]` attributes in front of a `static` ctor). The C# function-pattern loop now runs a wrapped-modifier recovery step when the regex fails on the raw line: `TryFindCSharpWrappedHeaderModifier` walks backwards through preceding lines that only contain modifier keywords (and any leading attributes), and `CSharpWrappedHeaderModifierLineRegex` certifies each such line as modifier-only. When a match is synthesized by prepending the collected prefix and retrying the pattern, the name-line column continues to be the authoritative emission site so the symbol's `line` stays on the identifier row (not the modifier row), and the recorded `signature` is rebuilt as `"<prefix> <name-line header>"` so consumers still see the modifier chain (`static A()`, `public B()`, `static D()`, `public static E()`). `BuildCSharpPropertyMatchLine` — the multi-line field/property header merger — now also declines to merge when the starting physical line is a pure modifier line (matched by the new `CSharpWrappedHeaderModifierLineRegex`), which previously caused a phantom ctor emission anchored to the modifier line to duplicate alongside the correct name-line emission. Multi-modifier wrapped shapes (e.g. `public\nstatic\nP1() { ... }`) are also covered: the synthesized `"public static P1()"` line satisfies neither the ctor regex (which accepts only `unsafe` / `extern` between visibility and name) nor the static-ctor regex (which requires `static` first), so a new `EnumerateCSharpWrappedModifierCandidates` helper fans out retries to the full prefix, a `static`-only variant (for static-ctor), and a visibility-only variant (for the ctor regex). The full prefix is still used to rebuild `signature` so multi-modifier declarations persist as `public static P1() { X = 1; }` even when the matching regex variant saw only `static P1()`. Added five extractor regression tests that pin the previously-dropped shapes: `Extract_CSharp_WrappedStaticConstructor_EmitsOnceAtNameLine` locks `static\nA() { ... }` emission on the name line with signature containing `static A()`; `Extract_CSharp_WrappedInstanceConstructor_EmitsOnceAtNameLine` locks `public\nB() { ... }`; `Extract_CSharp_WrappedAllmanStaticConstructor_CapturesBody` locks `static\nF()\n{\n ...\n}` including the Allman body so `body_end_line` still spans the body; `Extract_CSharp_AttributedWrappedStaticConstructor_EmitsOnceAtNameLine` locks `[System.Obsolete]\nstatic\nD() { ... }` so attribute-then-modifier-then-name wrapping stays captured; `Extract_CSharp_MultiModifierWrappedConstructor_EmitsOnceAtNameLine` locks `public\nstatic\nE() { ... }` so multi-modifier wrapping emits once at the name line with signature containing `public static E()`. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #348.
- **C# plain-field scope gate is now column-aware, fixing phantom `property` locals and dropped same-line class fields (#400)** — `SymbolExtractor`'s C# plain-field pattern (added in #298) uses a "must sit directly inside a type body" gate to keep method-local `int local = 1;` declarations out of the symbol index. The gate was built from a single `bool[]` indexed by line number, so it only answered the question "is any byte on this line inside a type body?" That bucket was wrong on two different C# shapes the #298 regression suite never covered: (a) `public class C { public int X; }` on a single physical line — the gate evaluated the byte range from column 0, saw the line started outside any body (the `public class` keyword itself is outside its own body), and rejected the `public int X;` match even though by column it clearly sat between `{` and `}`, so the field was silently dropped from `symbols` / `definition` / `outline` / `inspect` / `unused` / `hotspots`; and (b) `public class Outer { public void M() { int local = 1; } }` — the gate saw bytes on the line inside a type body (the `public void M` portion) and accepted every same-line plain-field shape, so `int local = 1;` was emitted as a phantom `property local` symbol even though its column was inside a method body. The gate is now a new `CSharpTypeBodyScope` whose per-line transition list records every column where the "inside a class-like type body" state flips, built from the existing `StructuralLineMasker` brace output plus a dedicated `CSharpTypeBodyDeclarationMarker` regex that matches `\b(?:class|struct|interface|record)\b\s+\w`. `IsInsideTypeBodyAt(line, column)` binary-searches the transitions and returns the state at that exact column, so `public int X;` at column 18 on `public class C { public int X; }` resolves inside the class body and `int local = 1;` at column 30 on `public class Outer { public void M() { int local = 1; } }` resolves inside the method body and is rejected. Two related advance-path bugs surfaced while validating the gate and were fixed in the same change: the C# class-like advance (`class` / `struct` / `interface` / `enum` / `namespace`) previously jumped past the header's closing `}`, so `public class Outer { public class Inner { public int X; } }` scanned `Outer`'s header and then skipped the entire body, silently losing `Inner` and `X`; it now advances past the opening `{` instead, letting same-line nested types be scanned. And the `property` `BodyStyle.None` plain-field advance (the path that walks past `;` to find declarator-list tails) used to `continue` the scan loop even when the initializer-terminated signal (`matchEndedAtEquals`) or a populated `declaratorEntries` list already consumed the tail — so `private int _a = 1, _b, _c = 3;` re-matched `1, _b, _c =` as a bogus field with `return_type="1, _b,"`; it now breaks when either signal is set. The signature for `property` `BodyStyle.None` is now clamped to the end of the field's declaration statement — the top-level `;` with paren / bracket / brace depth tracking so initializer `{` / `;` cannot short-circuit the scan, or the position of the enclosing type body's closing `}` if that `}` is hit before a `;`. This still fixes the original `} }` containment problem (`public int X;` inside `class C { public int X; }` stops at `;` so same-line `ContainsSymbol` container resolution in `AssignContainers` still attaches `X` to `Inner` rather than `Outer`), but it also preserves the real declaration text for initializer-backed fields like `private int _x = 42;` — an earlier revision clamped to the regex match length and stored the signature as `private int _x =`, a user-visible regression in `inspect` / `definition` payloads. The same-line plain-field advance path is driven off the same statement-end scan: instead of breaking out of the same-line scan when the match ended at `=` or after a declarator list was expanded, the advance steps past the statement-terminating `;` and continues the same-pattern scan, so multiple same-line field statements such as `public int A = 1; public int B;` (previously dropped `B`) and `public int A, B; public int C;` (previously dropped `C`) are all captured. When the scanner hits an unbalanced `}` before a `;` the same-line scan breaks without setting `stopAfterFirstPatternMatch`, so later unrelated patterns on the same line still get a chance to run. The earlier `_a = 1, _b, _c = 3;` regression (where advancing to the match-end re-matched `1, _b, _c =` as a bogus field with `return_type="1, _b,"`) cannot recur because the advance now lands past the statement-terminating `;`. `CSharpTypeBodyDeclarationMarker` also excludes `enum` from the class-like alternation because an enum body is a list of constants — not arbitrary statements — and treating its body as a type body let column-aware matching accept the `[Obsolete] A = (int)B,` shape as a phantom field and reclassified previously-known enum-member rows as `property` symbols. The column-aware gate and the statement-end signature clamp both run on `patternMatchLine`, which for C# is `CollapseCSharpGenericTypeWhitespace` output — generic-angle whitespace is collapsed (`Dictionary<string, int>` → `Dictionary<string,int>`) so regex patterns match. That collapse shifts column positions away from the raw source, and two iter2 regressions surfaced: (a) `public class C<T1, T2>{int X;}` on one physical line dropped `X` because `IsInsideTypeBodyAt` received a collapsed column while `CSharpTypeBodyScope` was built from raw structural lines — the collapsed-space column resolved before the `{` transition and the gate rejected the field; (b) `public Dictionary<string, int> Map = new(); public int B;` on one line produced `Map` without its trailing `;` and `B` with a phantom leading `;`, because `FindCSharpPlainFieldStatementEnd` returned collapsed-space endpoints that were then used to slice the raw `line`. `CollapseCSharpGenericTypeWhitespace` now additionally emits a per-character `collapsedToRaw` map (length `collapsed.Length + 1`, final slot = `raw.Length` sentinel so exclusive-end indices translate safely); `BuildCSharpMatchLines` threads a per-line map array, `Extract` captures it alongside `csharpMatchLines`, and a new `TranslateCSharpCollapsedColumnToRaw` helper converts a collapsed column back to raw before `IsInsideTypeBodyAt` and before slicing `line` for the plain-field signature. Translation is only applied when `ReferenceEquals(patternMatchLine, csharpMatchLines[i])` holds (single-line case where the per-line map applies); multi-line merged field headers built by `BuildCSharpPropertyMatchLine` keep the pre-existing raw-slice behavior because their column domain is the merged string. When no generic-angle whitespace was actually collapsed the helper emits `null` and callers fall through to identity, so non-generic C# lines pay no extra allocation. An iter3 crash regression surfaced in the same-line plain-field advance path: when `BuildCSharpPropertyMatchLine` merged a multi-line header (`public Dictionary<string, int>` + `    Map = new(); public int B;`) into a combined candidate, the advance-past-`;` loop added for the single-physical-line `A = 1; B;` case still fired, but `absoluteStartColumn` now sat in the merged-string column domain. The second regex hit on that merged line (`public int B;` on the continuation row) then fed `BuildCSharpMultilineSignature` a `startColumn` greater than `lines[startLineIndex].Length`, and `cdidx index` crashed with `startIndex cannot be larger than length of string`. The advance loop is now gated to single-line candidates (`ReferenceEquals(patternMatchLine, csharpMatchLines[i])`): for multi-line merged candidates it breaks instead, letting the outer physical-line loop re-visit the continuation line and pick up any trailing same-line fields there. Added ten `SymbolExtractor` regression tests that pin the full repro set: `Extract_CSharp_SameLineClassBodyFieldIsCapturedAndLocalIsRejected` locks `public class C { public int X; }` captures both `C` and `X` with clean signatures while `public class Outer { public void M() { int local = 1; } }` captures `Outer` and `M` but emits no phantom `local`; `Extract_CSharp_SameLineMultipleFieldsAreAllCaptured` locks `public class C { public int A; public int B; public int C; }` emits all three fields with each signature trimmed to its own declaration; `Extract_CSharp_SameLineNestedClassAttachesFieldToInnerType` locks `Outer { Inner { public int X; } }` captures `Outer`, `Inner`, and `X` with `X.ContainerQualifiedName` ending in `.Inner` rather than `.Outer`; and `Extract_CSharp_SameLineCompactEnumMembersDoNotLeakAsFields` locks that `public enum Mode { [Obsolete] A = (int)B, C = 2 }` keeps the enum and its members without emitting phantom `property` symbols for the members; `Extract_CSharp_SameLineFieldWithInitializerFollowedByAnotherField` locks `public class Holder { public int A = 1; public int B; }` captures both `A` and `B` with intact signatures (`public int A = 1;` / `public int B;`) so the initializer-bearing field no longer stops the same-line scan; `Extract_CSharp_SameLineDeclaratorListFollowedByAnotherField` locks `public class Holder { public int A, B; public int C; }` captures three property rows (`A`, `B` via declarator expansion, and `C` from the next same-line statement) so declarator expansion no longer drops the following field; `Extract_CSharp_PlainFieldWithInitializerKeepsFullSignature` locks the stored signature of `private int _x = 42;` at `private int _x = 42;` so `inspect` / `definition` consumers never see the truncated `private int _x =` form again; `Extract_CSharp_SameLineGenericClassHeaderStillCapturesInnerField` locks that `public class C<T1, T2>{int X;}` still captures both the class and field `X` with signature `int X;` after the collapsed→raw column translation is applied; and `Extract_CSharp_SameLineGenericFieldSignatureKeepsTerminator` locks that `public class C { public Dictionary<string, int> Map = new(); public int B; }` emits `Map` with signature `public Dictionary<string, int> Map = new();` (trailing `;` retained) and `B` with signature `public int B;` (no phantom leading `;`) so the collapsed-space endpoints cannot reintroduce the `;`-shift that used to mangle generic-bearing same-line field pairs; and `Extract_CSharp_MultiLineFieldFollowedBySameLineFieldDoesNotCrash` locks that `public class C\n{\n    public Dictionary<string, int>\n        Map = new(); public int B;\n}` extracts both `Map` and `B` without throwing, so the iter3 crash (where the same-line advance continued past the first `;` with a merged-candidate column and then fed `BuildCSharpMultilineSignature` a `startColumn` beyond `lines[i].Length`) cannot reappear. An iter4 interaction with #349's ctor-regex lookahead also surfaced during the merge-with-main: because this change no longer sets `stopAfterFirstPatternMatch` on plain-field property matches, the ctor regex now runs on lines the plain-field pattern already claimed, so same-line plain-field shapes with a modifier + tuple return — `public readonly (int, int) ? F4 = null;` (initialized) and `public readonly (int, int) ? F5;` (uninitialized) — fell through #349's lookahead (which only covered `[{(]|=>`) and re-emitted the phantom `function readonly` ctor rows that #349 was supposed to reject. The #349 ctor-regex negative lookahead terminator set is therefore extended from `[{(]|=>` to `[{(;]|=>|=(?![=>])` so plain fields terminated by `;` or initialized with `=` (excluding `==` and `=>`) are also rejected by the ctor regex; the existing `Extract_CSharp_ContextualKeywordWithWhitespacedTupleSuffix_DoesNotLeakCtorRegexPhantom` regression already pins these plain-field shapes, and `Extract_CSharp_CtorRegex_StillCapturesAllValidCtorForms` confirms real ctors (including `: base(...)` / `: this(...)` / `extern` ending in `;` / tuple-parameter / multi-line) are unaffected because a ctor has no identifier between the closing `)` and the body opener. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #400.
- **CJK queries no longer return 0 results against longer FTS tokens (#198)** — `fts_chunks` is created with FTS5's default `unicode61` tokenizer, which has no rule for splitting runs of adjacent CJK / Japanese / Chinese / Korean codepoints, so a multi-character CJK word like `計算する` is stored as a single FTS token. The literal-safe search path used to wrap every whitespace-separated query token in `"..."` phrase quotes without any prefix designator, so `cdidx search 計算` became `MATCH '"計算"'` and returned 0 matches against any chunk containing `計算する`, even though the text was clearly present — including against cdidx's own Japanese documentation (CLAUDE.md / README / CHANGELOG Japanese sections). `SanitizeFtsQuery` now routes each token through a new `FormatFtsToken` helper that detects CJK script codepoints via `Rune.EnumerateRunes()` and emits the token as an FTS5 prefix phrase (`"計算"*`) instead of a bare phrase, so `search 計算` now finds `def 計算する(値):` while pure-ASCII queries keep their existing exact-phrase semantics unchanged. The CJK set covers: Hiragana + Katakana + phonetic extensions + Kana Supplement + Kana Extended-A + Small Kana Extension (`U+1B000..U+1B16F`) + Kana Extended-B (`U+1AFF0..U+1AFFF`, Unicode 15.0); Bopomofo and Bopomofo Extended (Chinese phonetic / zhuyin, `U+3100..U+312F` and `U+31A0..U+31BF`); Han-script codepoints outside the Unified Ideographs blocks — ideographic iteration mark `々` (`U+3005`), closing mark `〆` (`U+3006`), number zero `〇` (`U+3007`), Hangzhou numerals (`U+3021..U+3029`), vertical kana repeat marks (`U+3031..U+3035`), and Hangzhou 10/20/30 + vertical iteration marks (`U+3038..U+303B`); CJK Unified Ideographs + Extensions A–I + Compatibility; the historical East Asian scripts that Unicode places in or adjacent to the CJK blocks and that `unicode61` keeps as word characters, listed as individual Unicode-block envelopes so regression tests exercise each block separately and a future narrowing of one block cannot drag the others — Yi Syllables (`U+A000..U+A48F`, the Nuosu syllabary), Tangut (`U+17000..U+187FF`), Tangut Components (`U+18800..U+18AFF`), Khitan Small Script (`U+18B00..U+18CFF`), Tangut Supplement (`U+18D00..U+18D8F`), and Nüshu (`U+1B170..U+1B2FF`, the non-BMP women's script historically used in Jiangyong County, Hunan); the individual iteration / annotation codepoints in the Ideographic Symbols and Punctuation block (`U+16FE0..U+16FF1`) that annotate Han-based historical text — Tangut Iteration Mark `U+16FE0` (`Lm`), Nüshu Iteration Mark `U+16FE1` (`Lm`), Old Chinese Iteration Mark `U+16FE3` (`Lm`), Khitan Small Script Filler `U+16FE4` (`Mn`), and Vietnamese Chu Nom Alternate Reading Marks CA / NHAY `U+16FF0..U+16FF1` (`Mc`) — with `U+16FE2` (Old Chinese Hook Mark, `Po`) intentionally excluded because `unicode61` drops it during tokenization, and Yi Radicals (`U+A490..U+A4CF`) intentionally excluded because every codepoint there is Unicode category `OtherSymbol` (`So`) and is dropped by `unicode61` during tokenization. `OtherNotAssigned` (`Cn`) is deliberately not excluded at the top: .NET's Unicode tables lag the Unicode Consortium's releases, so codepoints like the Extension I range `U+2EBF0..U+2EE5F` (Unicode 15.1, assigned 2023) still report `Cn` on .NET 8 — rejecting `Cn` up front would silently regress real CJK codepoints just because the runtime has not caught up. SQLite's bundled `unicode61` tokenizer also ships its own (different and older) Unicode tables, and empirical verification through the locally built binary on .NET 8 confirms that codepoints which .NET reports as `Cn` inside the block envelopes above — including Tangut's reserved `U+187F8..U+187FF`, Khitan's reserved `U+18CD6..U+18CFF`, and Tangut Supplement's reserved `U+18D09..U+18D8F` — are still kept as word characters by `unicode61` during indexing. Allowing these codepoints through the block-envelope branches therefore produces correct behavior: if a file genuinely contains `<hole-codepoint>abc`, `search <hole-codepoint>` returns that file; if it does not, FTS5 simply returns zero rows. That is the same #198 invariant that protects the assigned codepoints; Hangul syllables + Jamo blocks; and Halfwidth forms from halfwidth Katakana through halfwidth Hangul (`U+FF65..U+FFDC`). The predicate is deliberately CJK-scoped rather than "any non-ASCII codepoint": symbol Unicode categories (`OtherSymbol` / `MathSymbol` / `CurrencySymbol` / `ModifierSymbol`) are excluded up front so an emoji-adjacent CJK block cannot trigger fallback, and Latin-diacritic (`naïve`, `café`), Greek, Cyrillic, and emoji-mixed tokens skip the CJK prefix path. The narrowing matters because `unicode61` tokenizes Latin-diacritic normally (so prefix fallback would silently widen `naïve` to `naïvety` / `naïveness`), and `unicode61` also drops symbol codepoints entirely — promoting `foo🎉` to `"foo🎉"*` would be parsed by FTS5 as `"foo"*` and leak into unrelated ASCII neighbors like `foobar`, which an earlier round of this fix had actually regressed before codex review caught it. The halfwidth range intentionally stops at `U+FFDC` because `U+FFDD..U+FFDF` are unassigned and `U+FFE0..U+FFEE` are fullwidth currency / arrow symbols that `unicode61` drops during tokenization, while fullwidth Latin / digits (`ＡＢＣ`, `０１２`) sit earlier in the block and keep exact-phrase semantics. CJK Radicals Supplement (`U+2E80..U+2EFF`) and Kangxi Radicals (`U+2F00..U+2FDF`) are intentionally excluded from the CJK set because every codepoint in those blocks is Unicode category `OtherSymbol` (`So`) and is therefore dropped by `unicode61` during tokenization — prefix fallback cannot help them even if enabled. The same path is shared by `search`, the `--count` fast path (`CountSearchResults`), and the MCP `search` tool, so CLI and MCP consumers get the fix together. Important FTS-level semantics that callers should be aware of (documented rather than "fixed" here): (i) CJK tokens always take the prefix path, so `search 計算する` also returns chunks containing `計算する追加` — this is the intentional trade-off that makes `search 計算` work, and strict equality requires `--exact` / `instr`; (ii) emoji-mixed tokens cannot be distinguished from their plain ASCII counterpart at the FTS layer because `unicode61` strips the emoji on both the index side and the query side (`foo🎉` is indexed and queried as the token `foo`), so `search foo🎉` will match a file containing `def foo():` — strict emoji-bearing equality again requires `--exact`. Added `DbReaderTests` coverage for CJK substring matches via both `Search` and `CountSearchResults`, a positive pin that CJK full-token queries still find exact full-token matches, a paired pin that locks the intentional CJK full-token widening so it cannot be silently reverted into the #198 zero-hit repro, a "CJK prefix does not match unrelated CJK tokens" regression so `search 計算` never leaks into `検索する`, an emoji-mixed regression that pins `search foo🎉` against prefix widening into `foobar`, a companion emoji-mixed pin that documents the `foo🎉` / `foo` FTS indistinguishability and proves the `--exact` path does distinguish them, a Latin-diacritic regression that pins `search naïve` against widening into `naïvety`, non-BMP regressions for CJK Extension H (`U+31350`) and Extension I (`U+2EBF0`) so a predicate that walked chars instead of runes or forgot either range would fail its own dedicated test, and additional regressions for `々` (`U+3005`), `〇` (`U+3007`), halfwidth Hangul (`ﾱ` `U+FFA1`), Kana Extended-B (`𚿰` `U+1AFF0`), vertical kana repeat marks (`〱` `U+3031`), Bopomofo (`ㄅ` `U+3105`), Bopomofo Extended (`ㆠ` `U+31A0`), Yi Syllables (`ꀀ` `U+A000`), Tangut (`𗀀` `U+17000`), Tangut Components (`𘠀` `U+18800`), Khitan Small Script (`𘬀` `U+18B00`), Tangut Supplement (`𘴀` `U+18D00`), Nüshu (`𛅰` `U+1B170`), and the Ideographic Symbols and Punctuation iteration / annotation marks — Tangut Iteration Mark (`𖿠` `U+16FE0`, `Lm`), Khitan Small Script Filler (`𖿤` `U+16FE4`, `Mn`), and Vietnamese Chu Nom Alternate Reading Mark CA (`𖿰` `U+16FF0`, `Mc`) — each pinning `search <codepoint>` against a chunk containing `<codepoint>abc` to lock the #198 zero-hit shape on every new codepoint class we brought into the CJK set. The four Tangut-family tests (Tangut, Tangut Components, Khitan Small Script, Tangut Supplement) each exercise their own predicate branch so a future rewrite that collapses two of these blocks together breaks its own dedicated test first, and the three Ideographic Symbols and Punctuation tests span the `Lm`, `Mn`, and `Mc` Unicode categories so no individual annotation-category regression can silently slip past. Known follow-up (out of scope for this fix): emoji substring search (`search 🎉`) is still 0-result because the default `unicode61` categories `L* N* Co` exclude `S*` (symbols) entirely, so emoji are dropped by the tokenizer before any query ever runs. That requires a schema-level tokenizer change (issue #198 Option A/B) and is tracked separately. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSearchReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolDefinitions.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`, `CLAUDE.md`. Closes #198.
- **Regression lock for C# interpolated and verbatim string reference extraction (#264)** — The original issue report alleged that `ReferenceExtractor` hid call-site references inside C# `$"..."` interpolation holes and leaked phantom references from `@"..."` verbatim string bodies. On the current `StructuralLineMasker` implementation the C# paths already handle single-line `$"..."`, multi-line `$@"..."` / `@$"..."`, and non-interpolated `@"..."` correctly — interpolation-hole call sites are captured with correct `ContainerName`, and multi-line verbatim bodies never leak phantom edges — but no regression test pinned that behavior end-to-end for the exact fixture in the issue report, so any future refactor of the masker's C# frame-stack handling could silently reintroduce the bug. Added `Extract_CsharpInterpolatedAndVerbatimStrings_Issue264_Repro_CapturesHoleCallsAndSuppressesPhantoms` which feeds the issue's exact fixture (`$"Hello {Helper.GetName()}"`, `$"Age: {Helper.GetAge()} years"`, `$"Nested {Helper.Format(Helper.GetName())}"`, a multi-line `$@"..."` with an interpolation hole, a plain non-interpolated call site, and a multi-line `@"..."` verbatim body containing `PhantomCall()` / `PhantomTable()` / `MoreFake()`) through `ReferenceExtractor.Extract` and pins four invariants at once: `Helper.GetName` is captured exactly four times, `Helper.GetAge` and `Helper.Format` are each captured at least once, every captured call's `ContainerName` resolves to `Work`, and no reference row ever surfaces for the phantom identifiers embedded in the verbatim body. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #264.
- **C# nested `new interface` (member-hiding a base-class nested interface) is now pinned by a dedicated regression (#376)** — Issue #376 reported that `public new interface INested { ... }` nested inside a derived class was silently dropped because the C# interface regex modifier list was `(?:partial|unsafe)` and did not include `new`. The free-modifier-order rewrite for #355 already widened the list to `(?:partial|unsafe|file|new)`, so the current binary already emits two `interface INested` symbols — one nested in `Base`, one nested in `Derived` — and the #376 repro is no longer reproducible. This change locks that behavior in with a dedicated `Extract_CSharp_NewNestedInterface_MemberHiding` regression that runs the exact fixture from the issue and asserts both nested interfaces are extracted (`ContainerName == "Base"` and `ContainerName == "Derived"`), so a future modifier-list edit cannot regress the #376 case without a failing test. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #376.
- **C# contextual-keyword modifier + tuple-suffix return no longer emits phantom `function partial` / `function required` / `function readonly` rows (#349)** — Lines shaped like `public <MODIFIER> (TupleOrTupleSuffix) Name` were being claimed by the constructor regex `^\s*<visibility>\s+\w+\s*\(` with the modifier keyword itself (`partial`, `required`, `readonly`, etc.) captured as the constructor name whenever the method / property regex failed earlier (for example because the property regex could not consume a tuple return followed by `{`). The resulting phantom `function <MODIFIER>` rows polluted `symbols`, `definition`, `outline`, `hotspots`, and `unused`, and the real member (`P1`, `R1`, ...) was silently dropped alongside them. The constructor regex now adds a negative lookahead immediately after the opening `(` that rejects lines whose matching `)` is followed by an identifier + `{` / `(` / `=>` (with optional `?` / `[]` / `[,]` / whitespaced tuple suffixes in between, such as `(int, int) []` / `(int, int) ?` / `(int, int)  ?`) — the exact shape of a property / expression-bodied method with a modifier keyword. The suffix alternatives are factored into a shared `CSharpTupleSuffixPattern` constant now consumed by both `CSharpTypePattern` and the ctor lookahead so the two stay in lock-step and future tuple-suffix shapes only need to be added in one place. Real constructors (whose closing `)` is followed by `{` / `:` / `=>` / `;` / end-of-line, or is on a later line in a multi-line signature) are unaffected, including `: base(...)` / `: this(...)` initializers, `extern` declarations ending in `;`, tuple-parameter ctors, and multi-line signatures. Using a positional check instead of a keyword deny-list also preserves support for ctors whose name happens to collide with a contextual keyword spelling. Added `Extract_CSharp_ContextualKeywordWithTupleSuffixReturn_DoesNotLeakCtorRegexPhantom` regression coverage that pins no `function partial` / `function required` / `function readonly` phantoms and that real `P1` / `P2` / `R1` / `R2` / `M` members are captured with the correct kind, plus `Extract_CSharp_ContextualKeywordWithWhitespacedTupleSuffix_DoesNotLeakCtorRegexPhantom` that pins the whitespaced-suffix forms (`(int, int) []`, `(int, int) ?`, `(int, int)  ?`) stay phantom-free while `R4` / `F4` / `M3` / `P5` / `M4` emit under the correct kind, and `Extract_CSharp_CtorRegex_StillCapturesAllValidCtorForms` that locks in every major realistic ctor form (brace body, expression body, `: base(...)` / `: this(...)` initializers, `extern` with `;` termination, multi-line signature, tuple parameter) so a future tightening of the lookahead cannot silently regress real ctor extraction. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #349.
- **C# 8 `readonly` instance indexers on structs are now captured as `Item` symbols (#352)** — `SymbolExtractor` previously dropped `public readonly int this[int i] => _arr[i];` and `public readonly string this[string key] { get => key; }` silently, so `definition`, `symbols`, `outline`, and `inspect` undercounted `readonly`-heavy slice / span / immutable-wrapper struct surfaces. The indexer row already accepts `readonly` in the free-order modifier slot alongside `unsafe` / `extern` / `ref (readonly)` following the #355 rewrite, and this change locks that behavior in with a dedicated `Extract_CSharp_DetectsReadonlyIndexers` regression covering expression-body, block-body, and generic-return (`public readonly T this[int i] { get => _items[i]; }`) shapes plus non-readonly / readonly-method baselines so a future regex refactor cannot regress the #352 case without a failing test. Affected: `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`.
- **`cdidx search` now caps per-line snippet width, so a single match in a minified / transpiled file no longer returns hundreds of KB of output (#196)** — `cdidx search --snippet-lines N` already limited the *number* of snippet lines returned per result, but it did not cap the *width* of each individual line. A match inside a minified / transpiled single-line file (one ~120 KB physical line), a generated fixture, or an obfuscated payload therefore returned the entire raw line verbatim — JSON output ballooned to hundreds of KB per result, human TUI output wrapped unreadably, the MCP `search` tool's `structuredContent` blew up AI token budgets, and the issue's repro (a 120,009-char Python line with one match) returned the full 120 KB payload even with `--snippet-lines 1`. `SearchSnippetFormatter` now runs every snippet line through the shared `LineWidthFormatter.ClampLine` helper already used by `find` / `references` / `excerpt` / `inspect`, so match lines are clamped around the first match token (keeping the token visible with surrounding `...(+N)...` markers) and non-match context lines head-clamp with a trailing `...(+N)...` marker. `SearchHighlight` now carries `OriginalLineLength` and `Truncated` fields so AI clients can detect clamped lines, and `CompactSearchResult` / `SearchSnippetExcerpt` expose a `TruncatedLineCount` summary field. The new `--max-line-width <n>` flag (CLI) and `maxLineWidth` argument (MCP `search`) share the exact same contract and defaults as the other commands (`DefaultMaxLineWidth=512`, `MaxAllowedLineWidth=4096`), so users and AI clients don't have to remember a separate knob for `search`. `--max-line-width` is added to the search usage line, help description, and bash / zsh / fish completions (fish already emitted `search` as a subcommand but previously did not advertise `--max-line-width` for it). The bash and zsh `search` completion branches are also realigned with the actual `RunSearch` contract — `--exact-name` (which `RunSearch` rejects with a usage error) is dropped from the candidate set, and the accepted `--top` (a `--limit` alias) and `--no-dedup` flags are added. The MCP `maxLineWidth` helper now also fails closed on values above `MaxAllowedLineWidth` (schema ceiling `4096`) instead of silently clamping them, so a schema-violating `maxLineWidth: 4097` now surfaces as an explicit tool error rather than a silently rewritten success. The CLI `--max-line-width` parser matches the same contract on `search` / `references` / `inspect` / `excerpt` (via `ParseArgs`) and `find` (via `ValidateFindArgs`): values above `MaxAllowedLineWidth` now abort with `UsageError` and empty stdout instead of silently falling back to `ClampMaxLineWidth`, so CLI and MCP agree on the ceiling contract that automation depends on. For `find` in particular, `ValidateFindArgs` is now inline-`=` aware — it uses `TrySplitInlineOptionValue` to read an inline `--opt=value` token as `(--opt, value)` for its own validation without rewriting the arg list, so the pre-flight validator no longer rejects the documented `--opt=<value>` form with `unsupported option for find: --max-line-width=4097` while the other query commands accept it through `ParseArgs`. The arg list passed on to `ParseArgs` is left untouched, so legitimate inline values that themselves start with `--` (e.g. `--path=--literal.txt` for a path literally named `--literal.txt`, exactly the shape the existing CLI hint recommends) are preserved verbatim for `ParseArgs` to handle. Smoke-tested against the issue's repro: a 120,009-char single-line file with one match now produces ~293 bytes of output by default, ~137 bytes at `--max-line-width 200`, and ~2085 bytes at `--max-line-width 4096`; the JSON `snippet` field carries the `...(+119914)...` marker around the first match token, and `truncated_line_count` / `highlights[].truncated` / `highlights[].original_line_length` are populated. Short lines that fit within `maxLineWidth` are unchanged. Added `SearchSnippetFormatter` regression tests pinning the long-match-line clamp, long non-match-line clamp, `CompactSearchResult` truncation metadata, and the "short line stays verbatim" guarantee, updated the `ConsoleUi` usage and help-text assertions, and added a `QueryEntrypoints_MaxLineWidthAboveCeilingFailClosed_Issue196` theory that drives `RunSearch` / `RunReferences` / `RunInspect` / `RunFind` / `RunExcerpt` with `--max-line-width 4097` (and `search` with `8192`) and pins the `UsageError` exit, empty stdout, the explicit `"--max-line-width must be less than or equal to 4096"` stderr message, and the `Usage:` line, with matching inline-`=` rows (`--max-line-width=4097`) for `search` / `references` / `inspect` / `find` / `excerpt` so the inline-`=` validator contract is pinned alongside the space-separated form, plus a `RunFind_PathFilterAcceptsRecognizedOptionTokenViaInlineValue` regression that drives `find Alpha --db=<db> --path=--json-dir --count --json` end to end and pins that `find` honors inline `--path=<value>` values starting with `--`, matching the `search` / `files` contract. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/SearchSnippetFormatter.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/ConsoleUi.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolDefinitions.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SearchSnippetFormatterTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ConsoleUiTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/McpServerTests.cs`. Closes #196.
- **Common language-specific filenames and extensions are no longer silently dropped from the index (#189)** — `FileIndexer.TryDetectLanguage` previously only mapped a handful of extensions and exact filenames, so everyday files that real projects ship — Ruby's `Gemfile` / `Rakefile` / `Podfile` / `Guardfile` / `Capfile` / `.rake` / `.gemspec` / `.podspec`, Podman's `Containerfile`, explicit `GNUmakefile`, Makefile variants `Makefile.common` / `Dockerfile.dev`, Bazel `BUILD` / `BUILD.bazel` / `WORKSPACE` / `WORKSPACE.bazel` (indexed as Python because Starlark is a Python dialect), Python stubs and Windows launcher scripts `.pyi` / `.pyw` (mapped to `python`), Cython `.pyx` / `.pxd` (mapped to their own `cython` bucket — search-only, because `cdef class` / `cpdef` / `cdef` are not parsed by the Python symbol extractor and advertising them as `python` would claim `symbol_extraction=true` while emitting zero symbols, the same mismatch that sunk the earlier `.sass` / `.styl` → `css` mapping), T-SQL / PostgreSQL / Oracle PL/SQL dialects `.tsql` / `.pgsql` / `.plsql` / `.psql`, `.htm`, CSS-family preprocessors `.less` / `.pcss` (mapped to `css`), indentation-based Sass `.sass` and Stylus `.styl` (mapped to their own `sass` / `stylus` buckets because the CSS symbol extractor is brace-based and cannot parse indented syntax — they are search-only, matching the current `cdidx languages` `symbol_extraction` contract), and plain `.mk` — were all treated as binary/unknown and skipped without a shebang fallback match. `LangMap` has been extended with the missing extensions, `FileNameMap` with the missing exact-match filenames, and a new `FileNamePrefixMap` handles the `Dockerfile.<suffix>` / `Containerfile.<suffix>` / `Makefile.<suffix>` / `GNUmakefile.<suffix>` pattern that is idiomatic on real Dockerfile and GNU Make projects. The prefix match requires a non-empty suffix (`fileName.Length > prefix.Length`) so bare trailing-dot inputs like `Dockerfile.` remain unrecognized rather than being misclassified, and the prefix check runs after the exact-filename check so existing `Dockerfile` / `Makefile` / `GNUmakefile` rows keep their original language mapping. Extension lookup still runs first so tool-specific extensions like `.gemspec` are not shadowed by an accidental `.rb`-style prefix collision. `GetLanguageExtensions()` — the public API behind `cdidx languages` and the MCP language listing — now also surfaces the prefix variants as `<Prefix><suffix>` pseudo-entries (`Dockerfile.<suffix>`, `Containerfile.<suffix>`, `Makefile.<suffix>`, `GNUmakefile.<suffix>`) so the advertised language list matches what `TryDetectLanguage` actually recognizes at scan time. Added `FileIndexer` regression coverage that pins every new extension, every new exact filename, every prefix variant, an end-to-end `ScanFiles` test that constructs all 10 files from the issue's repro and asserts exactly 10 files come back indexed (previously only 1 survived), a negative theory that locks `Dockerfile.` / `Containerfile.` / `Makefile.` / `GNUmakefile.` bare trailing-dot inputs out of the prefix map, and a dedicated `GetLanguageExtensions_ExposesPrefixAndFileNameVariants` test that pins the exact-name and prefix-variant entries plus the `sass` / `stylus` split away from `css`. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `README.md`. Closes #189.
- **`cdidx languages` human-readable table no longer lets long extension lists swallow the `Symbols` / `Graph` columns** — `QueryCommandRunner.RunLanguages` formatted each row with a fixed-width `{exts,-36}` column, so languages whose extension list was wider than 36 characters (`python` with Bazel `BUILD` files, `ruby` with `Gemfile` / `Rakefile` / `Vagrantfile`, `xml` with the MSBuild `.csproj` / `.props` / `.targets` family, and — after the #189 follow-up — `dockerfile` and `makefile` with their `<Prefix><suffix>` pseudo-entries) pushed the `Symbols` and `Graph` cells to the right of the Extensions string, where they visually merged with the extension list and became unreadable on narrow terminals. The latent regression was invisible in test coverage because `RunLanguages_JsonListsModernNodeModuleExtensions` only exercised the `--json` path. Long rows now spill the extension list onto a `  Extensions: ...` continuation line while short rows keep the existing single-line table, and a new regression test `RunLanguages_HumanOutput_WideExtensionListSpillsOntoContinuationLine` pins the behavior for every currently-wide language (including the `Dockerfile.<suffix>` / `Containerfile.<suffix>` / `Makefile.<suffix>` / `GNUmakefile.<suffix>` pseudo-entries) so future additions do not silently reintroduce the layout break. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`.
- **C#/Java `nameof(X.Y)` / `typeof(T)` / `default(T)` / `T.class` arguments are indexed as `type_reference` edges (#253)** — The shared `CallRegex` in `ReferenceExtractor` requires a trailing `(` to emit a call edge, so the arguments of C# `nameof(Target.Alpha)`, `typeof(Target)`, `sizeof(Target)`, `default(Target)`, and Java `Target.class` never matched and silently disappeared from `references`, `inspect`, and `impact`. The C# path now uses a regex only to locate the `nameof` / `typeof` / `sizeof` / `default` keyword and its opening `(`, then walks the argument body with a small lexer that skips generic `<...>` / array `[...]` / tuple `(...)` groups and `global::` / `Alias::` namespace-alias qualifiers so nested paths like `nameof(List<int>.Count)`, `nameof(System.Collections.Generic.Dictionary<string, int>.KeyCollection)`, and `nameof(global::System.String)` are captured end-to-end instead of truncating at the first `<` or stopping at the `Alias` token. The Java path keeps a regex-based match against `<ident>(.ident)*\s*(\[\s*\])*\.class` and splits dotted arguments. Each segment is emitted with `reference_kind='type_reference'` so call-graph tools that only care about invocations are not polluted. Each row carries the original column and context line, Java primitive segments (`int`, `long`, `short`, `boolean`, `byte`, `char`, `float`, `double`, `void`) and C# predefined-type alias segments (`bool`, `byte`, `sbyte`, `short`, `ushort`, `int`, `uint`, `long`, `ulong`, `nint`, `nuint`, `char`, `float`, `double`, `decimal`, `string`, `object`, `void`, `dynamic`, `var`) are filtered out because they resolve to BCL primitives rather than indexed user-defined symbols, and the shared ignore-call set is also applied. C# bare `default;` (no `(`) is intentionally not captured. On the read side, `DbReader.GetCallers` / `CountCallers` / `CountCallersTotal` / `GetCallees` / `CountCallees` / `CountCalleesTotal` now exclude `reference_kind='type_reference'` rows whenever `referenceKind == null`, so `callers`, `callees`, and `impact` do not regress on the new edges; `subscribe` edges continue to surface in default caller/callee output to preserve existing event-subscription semantics (pinned by existing `DbReaderTests`). `references` and `--kind type_reference` still surface the new edges. Added regression coverage for C# `nameof` / `typeof` / `default` argument segments (including multi-level dotted arguments, generic stripping mid-path, nested generics, `global::` / alias qualifiers, C# built-in-alias skipping, tuple element capture across inner parens such as `typeof((Foo, Bar))` / `default((Foo, Bar))` / `typeof((Foo, Bar)[])`, and bare-`default` negative), the column alignment of each segment against the original source line, and Java `T.class` / `outer.inner.class` / primitive skipping, bracket skipping, and the full chain. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/ReferenceExtractor.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/ReferenceExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #253.
- **`--since` thresholds with a time-of-day component silently returned zero results (#203)** — `cdidx files --since 2025-06-20T21:00:00Z`, `cdidx symbols --since ...`, `cdidx search ... --since ...`, `cdidx definition --count --since ...`, and every other command layered on the `ListFiles` / `CountListFiles` / `SearchSymbols` / `CountSearchSymbols` / `CountSearchSymbolsTotal` / `CountDefinitionsTotal` / `Search` / `CountSearchResults` / `ScopeMayIncludeCSharpFiles` read paths returned zero rows whenever the threshold carried a non-midnight time-of-day, even when matching files with later `modified` timestamps existed in the index. All nine of those read paths bound the `@since` SQL parameter via `since.Value.ToString("O")`, producing the ISO-8601 round-trip format `yyyy-MM-ddTHH:mm:ss.fffffffZ` with a `T` separator and trailing `Z`. `files.modified` is written by `DbWriter` with a DateTime parameter, which Microsoft.Data.Sqlite stores as TEXT in its default `DateTimeSqliteDefaultFormat` — `yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm:ss.FFFFFFF` with a space separator and no `Z`. SQLite compares TEXT values lexicographically, and because `T` (0x54) is greater than ` ` (0x20) at position 10, `f.modified >= @since` was always false. All nine `@since` bindings now pass `since.Value` directly so the read path serializes through the same Microsoft.Data.Sqlite DateTime formatter used by the write path, which keeps the format symmetric regardless of future Microsoft.Data.Sqlite format changes. Added eight `DbReaderTests` regression tests covering every count route that the issue-era code path silently broke — `ListFiles_WithTimeOfDaySince_IncludesNewerFiles`, `CountListFiles_WithTimeOfDaySince_CountsOnlyNewerFiles`, `SearchSymbols_WithTimeOfDaySince_IncludesNewerFiles`, `Search_WithTimeOfDaySince_IncludesNewerFiles`, `ListFiles_WithTimeOfDaySince_ExcludesFilesBeforeThreshold`, `CountSearchResults_WithTimeOfDaySince_CountsOnlyNewerChunks`, `CountSearchSymbolsTotal_WithTimeOfDaySince_CountsOnlyNewerSymbols`, `CountDefinitionsTotal_WithTimeOfDaySince_CountsOnlyNewerDefinitions` — that insert files whose `modified` timestamp straddles a 21:00 UTC threshold and pin that `--since` correctly includes later files and excludes earlier ones on every fixed code path, with bilingual comments documenting the root cause so the invariant can't silently regress to the old `ToString("O")` path. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSearchReader.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbSymbolReader.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`. Closes #203.
- **`--lang` and `--kind` are now case-insensitive, and `WriteLangHint` now fires for `symbols` and `definition` (#199)** — `QueryCommandRunner.ParseArgs` previously stored `--lang` and `--kind` values verbatim, so `--lang Python` or `--kind FUNCTION` bypassed the SQL filters (every `files.lang` and `symbols.kind` row is lowercase) and returned 0 results. The same zero-result path on `symbols` and `definition` also skipped `WriteLangHint`, so users only saw the generic `try removing --lang, --path, ...` hint instead of the `'Python' not found in index. Available: python` hint that `search`, `references`, `callers`, `callees`, `inspect`, and `impact` already emit. `ParseArgs` now lowercases `--lang` / `--kind` at the parse site so every downstream SQL filter and hint comparison sees the normalized form, and `RunDefinition` / `RunSymbols` now call `WriteLangHint(options.Lang, reader)` alongside `WriteKindHint`, matching the other command surfaces. MCP `args["lang"]` / `args["kind"]` readers in `McpToolHandlers` apply the same lowercase normalization so MCP clients benefit from the same behavior. Added six regression tests in `QueryCommandRunnerTests`: `ParseArgs_NormalizesLangAndKindToLowercase` pins the parse-site normalization, `RunSymbols_AcceptsLangPythonCaseInsensitively` / `RunSymbols_AcceptsKindFunctionCaseInsensitively` / `RunDefinition_AcceptsLangPythonCaseInsensitively` pin that mixed-case values produce the same successful output as lowercase, and `RunSymbols_EmitsLangHintForUnknownLang` / `RunDefinition_EmitsLangHintForUnknownLang` pin the `Available: python` hint for unknown values. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Mcp/McpToolHandlers.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/QueryCommandRunnerTests.cs`. Closes #199.
- **`FileIndexer` no longer follows directory or file symlinks, preventing infinite recursion on ancestor loops and duplicate indexing (#190)** — `FileIndexer.EnumerateDirectory` previously enumerated subdirectories with a plain `Directory.EnumerateDirectories(dir)` and recursed unconditionally, with no reparse-point check and no visited-path tracking. A directory symlink pointing at an ancestor (e.g. `sub/parent_loop -> ..`) caused the indexer to walk `sub/parent_loop/sub/parent_loop/...` dozens of times until the OS path limit finally aborted recursion, indexing the same physical file under each synthetic path and polluting `symbols`, `files`, `outline`, `map` entrypoints while inflating index size. A milder symptom also affected file symlinks pointing at in-project files: the same content was indexed twice under two different paths. Both paths now check `FileAttributes.ReparsePoint` via a shared `IsReparsePoint` helper and skip symlinks without descending or reading. Directory symlinks are still recorded in `ListedDirectories` / `FullyScannedDirectories` so stale entries previously indexed under their synthetic paths get purged on the next full scan. Dangling symlinks (target missing) throw `FileNotFoundException` / `DirectoryNotFoundException` from `File.GetAttributes` and are treated as reparse points so the scan does not abort. The project root itself is unaffected — when the user explicitly points `cdidx index` at a symlinked directory, `_projectRoot` is used as the enumeration base, so the symlink is followed transparently by the OS. The reparse-point check also runs inside `GetFileIndexability`, so update paths (`cdidx index --files` / `--commits`), dry-run mode, and the Windows path all reject symlinks uniformly — `stat()`-based Unix probing would otherwise follow file symlinks silently and re-index the target under the link path. A new `SymlinkPrunedDirectories` set is threaded from `ScanFilesDetailed` through `ScanFilesResult` to `DbWriter.PurgeFilesOutsideRetainedSetWithinListedDirectories`, which now also purges deep descendants previously indexed under synthetic symlink ancestors (e.g. `sub/parent_loop/nested/a/b/c.py`) using a directory-boundary-safe `LastIndexOf('/')` ancestor walk, so re-indexing after an old loop-produced DB cleans up stale rows in one pass without collapsing sibling directories that happen to share a name prefix (`sub/parent_loop` vs `sub/parent_loop_sibling`). Added six regression tests: directory symlink to ancestor indexes once (not 40+ times), file symlink to in-project real file is deduplicated to a single row, a project containing only dangling file/directory symlinks still indexes the real files without aborting, `GetFileIndexability` rejects a file symlink so update-mode call paths skip it, deep descendants previously indexed under a symlink-pruned directory are purged on re-index, and the ancestor-walk prune does not confuse `sub/parent_loop` with sibling `sub/parent_loop_sibling/...`. Tests that create symlinks skip on Windows because creating symlinks there requires admin/developer mode. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Database/DbWriter.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DatabaseTests.cs`, `CLAUDE.md`. Closes #190.
- **C# declarations with non-canonical modifier order are no longer misclassified or dropped from symbol extraction (#355)** — C# grammar lets members and type declarations carry modifiers in any order (`public static readonly` ≡ `readonly public static` ≡ `static public readonly`, `public abstract class` ≡ `abstract public class`), but `SymbolExtractor` previously hard-coded visibility-first ordering on every C# row, so `readonly public static int E = 6;` fell through to the plain-field row and was emitted as kind `property` instead of kind `function` (losing the static readonly / const promotion), `static public int F() => 0;` lost its `visibility=public` (captured as empty), `abstract public class X {}` / `sealed public class Y {}` / `readonly public struct Z {}` / `ref public struct W {}` / `partial public interface I {}` were dropped entirely from `symbols` / `definition` / `outline` / `inspect`, `new public const int HiddenConst = 2;` (a compiler-legal same-name base-const hiding) was dropped from symbol extraction, and forms like `static public event System.EventHandler E1;` / `static public delegate int D1(int x);` / `static public int P1 { get; set; }` / `static public int this[int i] => 0;` / `static public explicit operator Money(...)` / `static public int operator +(...)` could drop or misclassify entirely. The affected rows — const field, static readonly field, conversion operator, operator overload, method (and its `delegate` negative-lookahead guard), brace-body property, expression-body property, delegate, event, indexer, interface, struct, class (including `record class` / `record`), and enum — now use a modifier alternation that accepts visibility at any position in the modifier sequence, and the static readonly field row uses two zero-width lookahead assertions (`(?=(?:...)*static\s+)` and `(?=(?:...)*readonly\s+)`) to enforce both keywords regardless of order (including `readonly new static`, `new readonly static`, and `static readonly new` interleaving). The method-row `delegate` negative lookahead is also widened to consume the same free-order modifier sequence, so real `public delegate int D(int x);` declarations continue to route to the dedicated delegate row and not get re-classified as methods. The plain-field (kind `property`) row is unaffected and still handles instance / readonly / volatile / plain static fields. Added five `SymbolExtractor` regression tests: `Extract_CSharp_StaticReadonlyField_FreeModifierOrder` pins seven orderings of the `static readonly` fixture (`public static readonly`, `public readonly static`, `public new static readonly`, `public readonly new static`, `public new readonly static`, `readonly public static`, `static readonly new`) as kind `function` and asserts none appear as kind `property`; `Extract_CSharp_Method_FreeModifierOrder` pins `static public`, `static internal`, `async public`, `override public`, and `virtual public` with the correct captured visibility; `Extract_CSharp_Property_ModifierBeforeVisibility` pins `static public int P1 { get; set; }`, `static public int P2 => 0;`, `virtual public int P3 { get; set; }`, `override public int P4 => 0;`, `static public event System.EventHandler E1;`, `static public delegate int D1(int x);`, and `static public int this[int i] => 0;` (indexer normalized to `Item` via `NormalizeCSharpSymbolName`); `Extract_CSharp_TypeDeclarations_FreeModifierOrder` pins `abstract public class`, `sealed public class`, `readonly public struct`, `ref public struct`, `partial public interface`, and `abstract public record class`; `Extract_CSharp_ConstField_FreeModifierOrder` pins `new public const int HiddenConst = 2;` and `public new const int HiddenConst2 = 3;` as kind `function` with `visibility=public` and `return_type=int`. The brace-body property, expression-body property, event, and indexer rows now also accept `unsafe` / `extern` in their free-order modifier sequence, the constructor row now accepts an `unsafe` / `extern` prefix either before or after the visibility token (`unsafe public S(int* p) {}` and `extern public S(int x);` previously captured with empty `visibility` and a polluted `return_type` that absorbed the leading modifier, or were dropped entirely for event / constructor shapes), and the static-constructor row now accepts `unsafe` before or after `static` (`unsafe static S()` ≡ `static unsafe S()`), so every compiler-legal `unsafe` / `extern` placement is captured with correct `visibility` and without the leading modifier bleeding into `return_type`. Added a sixth `SymbolExtractor` regression test `Extract_CSharp_UnsafeExtern_FreeModifierOrder` that pins `unsafe public` property (brace and expression body), `unsafe public` / `extern public` event, `unsafe public` indexer (normalized to `Item`), `unsafe public` / `extern public` constructors, and an `unsafe static` static constructor. The plain-field row and the multi-line field-header prefix regex (`CSharpPropertyHeaderPrefixRegex`) were also visibility-first and the header prefix did not accept `const`, so `static public int X;`, `readonly public int Y;`, the multi-line `static public Dictionary<string, int>` + `    Map = new();` shape, and the multi-line const `new public const int` + `    C = 1;` shape either dropped `visibility` or were dropped entirely from `symbols` / `definition` / `outline` / `inspect` / `unused`. Both regexes now accept visibility anywhere in the modifier sequence, the header prefix accepts `const` alongside the other field-eligible modifiers for the multi-line const case, and the field-header merger in `BuildCSharpPropertyMatchLine` now runs for both `property` and `function` kinds so `const` / `static readonly` field patterns (kind `function`) can see the merged header line. Non-field `function` patterns (methods, constructors, operators, indexers) are unaffected because `CSharpPropertyHeaderPrefixRegex` requires the line to end before `(` or `{`. Added a seventh regression test `Extract_CSharp_PlainField_FreeModifierOrder` covering `static public int X;`, `readonly public int Y;`, `new public static int Z = 1;`, the multi-line generic field, and the multi-line const. The event row also previously rejected the inheritance modifiers that are legal on event declarations per the C# spec (`virtual` / `override` / `abstract` / `sealed`), and the interface and delegate rows did not accept the `file` file-scoped type modifier (or `new` for nested delegate hiding), so `abstract public event System.EventHandler E;`, `virtual public event System.EventHandler E;`, `sealed public override event System.EventHandler E;`, `file interface I {}`, and `file delegate int D(int x);` were dropped from symbol extraction. The plain-field negative lookahead was also too narrow: because `abstract` / `virtual` / `override` / `sealed` / `async` / `partial` / `file` / `ref` were not in the rejected-leading-token list, a declaration like `abstract public event System.EventHandler A;` was matching the plain-field row with `return_type` absorbing `"abstract public event System.EventHandler"` and `visibility` left empty. Added `virtual` / `override` / `abstract` / `sealed` / `new` to the event modifier alternation, added `file` / `new` to the interface and delegate alternations, and added `abstract` / `virtual` / `override` / `sealed` / `async` / `partial` / `file` / `ref` to the plain-field negative lookahead so non-field leading modifiers can no longer bleed into `return_type`. Added an eighth regression test `Extract_CSharp_InheritanceAndFile_FreeModifierOrder` pinning `file interface`, `file delegate`, and four inheritance-modifier event forms (`abstract public`, `virtual public`, `sealed public override`, `new public`) with `visibility="public"`. Updated the C# language-pattern row in `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md` to note that modifier order is now accepted in any position. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`, `DEVELOPER_GUIDE.md`. Closes #355.
- **POSIX filenames containing `\` no longer become phantom `/` subdirectories in the index (#191)** — `FileIndexer.BuildRecordWithRawBytes` and several CLI helpers (`GitHelper.GetChangedFilesFromCommit`, `IndexCommandRunner` full-scan / `--commits` / `--files` path normalization and `.git/info/exclude` computation, `QueryCommandRunner.RunOutline`) unconditionally ran `Replace('\\', '/')` on relative paths regardless of the host OS. On Windows that is correct because `\` is the directory separator, but on POSIX `\` is a legal filename character (data-science notebooks with awkward names, generated / escaped paths, adversarial filenames) so a single-component file called `back\slash.py` was silently rewritten to `back/slash.py`. The file was then stored as if there were a `back/` directory containing `slash.py`, `excerpt 'back\slash.py'` and `outline back\slash.py` returned "No excerpt found" / null because the DB key was the mangled form, `files` / `map` / `outline` advertised a phantom `back/` subdirectory that does not exist on disk, and AI clients building mental maps from those outputs wasted tool calls exploring the imaginary directory. Added a single `FileIndexer.NormalizePathSeparators` helper that only runs the `\`→`/` conversion when `Path.DirectorySeparatorChar == '\\'` (i.e. on Windows), and replaced all nine storage and lookup sites so Windows indexes still normalize separators while POSIX indexes preserve `\` inside filenames verbatim. Internal pattern-matching helpers (`NormalizeIgnorePath` for gitignore rules, `NormalizeScopeKey` for ambiguous-project scope grouping) are intentionally left unchanged because they operate on gitignore-style patterns, not filesystem-literal paths. Added a POSIX-gated `BuildRecord_PreservesBackslashInPosixFilename` unit test that creates a `back\slash.py` file on disk and asserts `record.Path` is stored as `back\slash.py`, a `GetExcerptAndOutline_RoundTripPathContainingBackslash` DB-level regression that pins `excerpt` / `outline` lookups succeed against the literal path and fail against the mangled `back/slash.py` form, and cross-platform unit tests for `NormalizePathSeparators` itself covering both the Windows-separator and POSIX-no-op branches. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/FileIndexer.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/GitHelper.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/IndexCommandRunner.cs`, `src/CodeIndex/Cli/QueryCommandRunner.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/FileIndexerTests.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/DbReaderTests.cs`. Closes #191.
- **Multi-line C# enum members, JS/TS bare methods, and C# record primary-ctor headers no longer leak `\r` into signatures on CRLF sources (#405)** — `SymbolExtractor.GetSourceSpanText` (used to build C# enum member signatures via `TryAddCSharpEnumMemberFromSpan`), `TryCaptureJavaScriptTypeScriptMethodHeader` (used to build `Signature` for JS/TS class-body methods whose header wraps across physical lines), and `CollectRecordDeclarationText` (used internally to parse C# record primary-constructor components) all concatenated `lines[...]` slices with a literal `'\n'` separator without stripping the trailing `'\r'` that `content.Split('\n')` leaves on CRLF-terminated input. As a result, Windows / `autocrlf=true` / Visual Studio-saved sources produced signatures carrying OS-dependent `"\r\n"` between physical lines, breaking cross-OS signature equality, snapshot tests, and any downstream consumer that compared signatures by string equality. This is the same class of bug that `#382` fixed for `BuildCSharpTypeHeaderSignature`. All three paths now use a shared `StripTrailingCr` / `GetLineLengthExcludingTrailingCr` helper to drop one trailing `'\r'` per line before appending, so inter-line separators stay `'\n'` regardless of source line endings. For the JS/TS path, both the source builder and the sanitized builder strip in lockstep so the column-to-source mapping in `TryMapJavaScriptTypeScriptHeaderColumnToSourceLocation` stays aligned. Added three regression tests that construct CRLF-terminated content for each extractor path (a multi-line C# enum member span, a wrapped JS class-body method, and a wrapped C# record primary constructor) so the fix is pinned for every path. Bare-CR (old-Mac) line endings remain out of scope because `content.Split('\n')` does not split them at all. Affected: `src/CodeIndex/Indexer/SymbolExtractor.cs`, `tests/CodeIndex.Tests/SymbolExtractorTests.cs`. Closes #405.
- **Wrapped C# class / struct / interface / enum headers now preserve their base list and `where` clauses in `symbols.signature` (#382)** — `SymbolExtractor` previously sliced `SymbolRecord.Signature` for C# type declarations from the single physical line the declaration regex matched, so headers whose base list or generic constraints wrapped onto following lines — e.g. `public sealed class Foo<T>\n    : BaseFoo<T>, IBar, IBaz\n    where T : class, new()\n{` — truncated to `public sealed class Foo<T>` and silently lost every `:` base, interface, and `where T : ...` clause. Downstream consumers that read the signature to recover the base type (the planned `ParseCSharpBaseType` path in #257, future type-position reference extraction for #256, any lint or `impact` / `analyze_symbol` flow that wants to answer "what does this class extend?" from the index alone) degraded to "no base type" for every wrapped-header C# class on every large library that uses formatter-wrapped headers (ASP.NET Core, Roslyn, EF Core, xUnit, `Microsoft.Extensions.*`, etc.). The C# signature path now extends the existing multi-line-signature mechanism (already used for properties) to type declarations: a new `TryFindCSharpTypeHeaderExtent` helper scans forward from the header start using `LexCSharpLine` so `{` / `;` inside string literals, comments, and verbatim / raw strings are ignored, tracks paren depth (C# 12 primary constructor parameter lists) and bracket depth (attributes on type or generic parameters) so a nested `{` / `;` can never short-circuit the scan, terminates at the first body-opening `{` or primary-constructor / forward-declaration `;` at zero depth, and caps lookahead at 64 lines to stay safe on unterminated input. A dedicated `BuildCSharpTypeHeaderSignature` assembles the header slice by concatenating the relevant `[startColumn, endColumn)` span from each physical line with a literal `'\n'` between lines, then runs the combined text through a single-pass `SanitizeCSharpTypeHeaderSlice` that strips `//` line comments (terminated at the next `'\n'`) and `/* ... */` block comments, collapses runs of Code-mode whitespace (including the newlines between lines) into a single space, and preserves String / Verbatim / Raw / Char literal contents verbatim — including multi-line raw / verbatim strings, which keep every internal line break and leading indentation instead of being `Trim()`ed and space-joined. The sanitizer also tracks C# interpolation holes with an explicit frame stack: `$"..."`, `$@"..."`, `@$"..."`, `$"""..."""`, and `$$"""{{expr}}"""` each push a String / Verbatim / Raw frame marked `Interpolated`, and a hole opens only when the `{` run is at least as long as the number of `$` prefixes (with `{{` and `}}` still honored as literal-brace escapes in non-raw interpolated strings). Inside a hole, the sanitizer re-enters Code mode and matching nested braces before returning to the outer literal, so `$"{@"a  b"}  c"` now keeps the inner verbatim literal's double-space intact and the outer literal content `  c` is preserved instead of the previous collapse to `a b` + ` c`. The helper still produces signatures like `public sealed class Foo<T> : BaseFoo<T>, IBar, IBaz where T : class, new()` for plain wrapped headers, and literal-bearing declarations like `record Foo(string S = "a  b")`, `@"C:\tmp\   spaces"`, `"""a   b"""`, multi-line raw-string primary-constructor defaults, and interpolation holes containing nested verbatim strings all keep every internal space and newline exactly as written. Same-line headers, single-line bodies, and the existing multi-line property path are unchanged.
